      <p>This page is to <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:DYKTN#nominate" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:DYKTN">nominate</a> fresh articles to appear in the "<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:DYK" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:DYK">Did you know</a>" section on the <a href="/wiki/Main_Page" title="Main Page">Main Page</a>, by a "hook" (an interesting note). Nominations that have been approved are moved to a <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved" title="Template talk:Did you know/Approved">staging area</a>, from which the articles are promoted into <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know/Queue" title="Template:Did you know/Queue">the Queue</a>. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><i><big><span class="noprint plainlinks purgelink"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know&amp;action=purge"><span title="Purge this page">Click here to "purge" this page</span></a></span></big> (if it looks like updates to subsidiary templates aren't being reflected).</i></li>
      </ul>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Instructions_for_nominators">Instructions for nominators</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template:DYK_nomination_header&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-1" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1007196855">.mw-parser-output .module-shortcutboxplain{float:right;margin:0 0 0 1em;border:1px solid #aaa;background:#fff;padding:0.3em 0.6em 0.2em 0.6em;text-align:center;font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .module-shortcutboxleft{float:left;margin:0 1em 0 0}.mw-parser-output .module-shortcutlist{display:inline-block;border-bottom:1px solid #aaa;margin-bottom:0.2em}.mw-parser-output .module-shortcutboxplain>ul{font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .module-shortcutanchordiv{position:relative;top:-3em}.mw-parser-output li .module-shortcutanchordiv{float:right}.mw-parser-output .mbox-imageright .module-shortcutboxplain{padding:0.4em 1em 0.4em 1em;line-height:1.3}</style>
      <div class="module-shortcutanchordiv">
       <span id="WP:DYKNOM"></span>
      </div>
      <div class="module-shortcutboxplain plainlist noprint" role="note">
       <div class="module-shortcutlist">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Shortcut" title="Wikipedia:Shortcut">Shortcut</a>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wikipedia:DYKNOM&amp;redirect=no">WP:DYKNOM</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>Create a subpage for your new DYK suggestion and then list the page below under the <b>date the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:DYKTN#article" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:DYKTN">article</a> was created or the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:DYKTN#expansion" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:DYKTN">expansion</a> began or it became a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:DYKTN#good_article" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:DYKTN">good article</a></b> (<u><b>not</b></u> the date you submit it here), with the newest dates at the bottom. Any registered user may <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:DYKTN#nominate" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:DYKTN">nominate</a> a DYK suggestion (if you are not a registered user, please leave a message at the bottom of <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia_talk:DYK" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia talk:DYK">the DYK project talk page</a> with the details of the article you would like to nominate and the hook you would like to propose); <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:DYKTN#self-nom" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:DYKTN">self-nominations</a> are permitted and encouraged. Thanks for participating and please remember to check back for comments on your nomination (consider <a href="/wiki/Help:Watchlist" title="Help:Watchlist">watchlisting</a> your nomination page). </p> 
      <table role="presentation" class="metadata mbox-small" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" class="mbox-text"> 
          <div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">
           <b>Does this look too complicated?</b> 
           <br>Try this semi-automated process instead:
          </div></td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:DYK-helper_menu_option.png" class="image"><img alt="DYK-helper menu option.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/DYK-helper_menu_option.png/220px-DYK-helper_menu_option.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="131" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/DYK-helper_menu_option.png/330px-DYK-helper_menu_option.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/79/DYK-helper_menu_option.png 2x" data-file-width="392" data-file-height="233"></a></td> 
         <td class="mbox-text plainlist"></td>
        </tr> 
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" class="mbox-text">1. Install the user script <a href="/wiki/User:SD0001/DYK-helper" title="User:SD0001/DYK-helper">DYK-helper.js</a>. <p>2. Go back to the article, and choose the "DYK" menu from the "More" menu </p> 3. Fill in the form and submit it.</td>
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div style="text-align: center;">
       <i><b>If this is your first nomination, please read the DYK rules before continuing:</b></i>
      </div> 
      <div style="text-align: center;">
       <i>Official DYK criteria:</i> <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Did_you_know#DYK_rules" title="Wikipedia:Did you know">DYK rules</a></b> and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Did_you_know/Supplementary_guidelines" title="Wikipedia:Did you know/Supplementary guidelines">supplementary guidelines</a>
      </div> 
      <div style="text-align: center;">
       <i>Unofficial guide:</i> <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Did_you_know/Learning_DYK" title="Wikipedia:Did you know/Learning DYK">Learning DYK</a>
      </div> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="How_to_list_a_new_nomination"></span> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="To_nominate_an_article"><span class="anchor" id="How_to_post_a_new_nomination"></span>To nominate an article</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template:DYK_nomination_header&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-2" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="quotebox pullquote centered" style="width:50%; border-width: 0px; background-color: #E7E7E7;">
       <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1012376600">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style> 
       <div class="quotebox-title" style="background-color: #E7E7E7;">
        Read these instructions completely before proceeding.
       </div> 
       <div class="quotebox-quote center-aligned" style="">
        <i>For simplified instructions, see <a href="/wiki/User:Rjanag/Quick_DYK_2" title="User:Rjanag/Quick DYK 2">User:Rjanag/Quick DYK 2</a>.</i>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <table style="width:100%;"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td style="background-color:#ffff99"><span style="font-family:Verdana,Arial,serif"><b>I</b>.</span> </td> 
         <td>
          <div style="font-size:100%;width:12em;max-width:30%;float:left;margin:2px 0px 2px 0px;border:1px solid #ffcc00;padding:.1em;text-align:center;background-color:#ffff99;">
           Create the nomination subpage.
          </div> 
          <div style="clear:both;"></div> <p>Enter the article title in the box below and click the button. (To nominate multiple articles together, enter any or all of the article titles.) You will then be taken to a preloaded nomination page. </p> 
          <div class="mw-inputbox-centered" style="background-color: clear;">
           <form name="createbox" class="createbox" action="/w/index.php" method="get">
            <input type="hidden" value="edit" name="action">
            <input type="hidden" value="Template:T:TDYK/preload" name="preload">
            <input type="hidden" value="Template:T:TDYK/editintro" name="editintro">
            <input type="hidden" value="Template:Did you know nominations/" name="prefix">
            <input type="text" name="title" class="mw-inputbox-input mw-ui-input mw-ui-input-inline createboxInput" value="" placeholder="YOUR ARTICLE TITLE" size="50" dir="ltr">
            <br>
            <input type="submit" name="create" class="mw-ui-button mw-ui-progressive createboxButton" value="Create nomination">
           </form>
          </div> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="background-color:#ffcc00"><span style="font-family:Verdana,Arial,serif"><b>II</b>.</span> </td> 
         <td>
          <div style="font-size:100%;width:12em;max-width:30%;float:left;margin:2px 0px 2px 0px;border:1px solid #ffcc00;padding:.1em;text-align:center;background-color:#ffff99;">
           Write the nomination.
          </div> 
          <div style="clear:both;"></div> <p>On the nomination page, fill in the relevant information. See <a href="/wiki/Template:NewDYKnomination" title="Template:NewDYKnomination">Template:NewDYKnomination</a> and <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:NewDYKnomination/guide" title="Template:NewDYKnomination/guide">NewDYKnomination/guide</a>}}</code> for further information. </p> 
          <ul>
           <li>Not every line of the template needs to be filled in. For instance, if you are not nominating an image to appear with your hook, there is no need to fill in the image-related lines.</li> 
           <li>Add an edit summary e.g. "Nominating YOUR ARTICLE TITLE for DYK" and click <i>Save page</i>.</li> 
           <li>Make sure the nomination page is on your watchlist, so you can follow the review discussion.</li>
          </ul> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="background-color:orange"><span style="font-family:Verdana,Arial,serif"><b>III</b>.</span> </td> 
         <td>
          <div style="font-size:100%;width:12em;max-width:30%;float:left;margin:2px 0px 2px 0px;border:1px solid #ffcc00;padding:.1em;text-align:center;background-color:#ffff99;">
           Post at <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Template talk:Did you know</a>.
          </div> 
          <div style="clear:both;"></div> <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Did_you_know#Current_nominations" title="Template talk:Did you know">current nominations section</a> find the subsection for the <b>date on which the article was created or on which expansion began</b> (or, if a new Good Article, the <b>date on which it became a GA</b>), not the date on which you make the nomination. </p> 
          <ul>
           <li>At the <em>top</em> of that subsection (before other nominations already there, but below the section head and hidden comment) add <code>{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/YOUR_ARTICLE_TITLE" title="Template:Did you know nominations/YOUR ARTICLE TITLE">Did you know nominations/YOUR ARTICLE TITLE</a>}}</code>.</li> 
           <li>Add an edit summary e.g. "Nominating YOUR ARTICLE TITLE for DYK" and click <i>Save page</i>.</li>
          </ul> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="How_to_review_a_nomination">How to review a nomination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template:DYK_nomination_header&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-3" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main page: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Did_you_know/Reviewing_guide" title="Wikipedia:Did you know/Reviewing guide">Wikipedia:Did you know/Reviewing guide</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Any editor who was not involved in writing/expanding or nominating an article may review it by checking to see that the article meets all the DYK criteria (<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Did_you_know/Article_length" title="Wikipedia:Did you know/Article length">long enough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Did_you_know/New_article" title="Wikipedia:Did you know/New article">new enough</a>, no serious <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Did_you_know#contentrules" title="Wikipedia:Did you know">editorial or content issues</a>) and the hook is cited. Editors may also alter the suggested hook to improve it, suggest new hooks, or even lend a hand and make edits to the article to which the hook applies so that the hook is supported and accurate. For a more detailed discussion of the DYK rules and review process see the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Did_you_know/Supplementary_guidelines" title="Wikipedia:Did you know/Supplementary guidelines">supplementary guidelines</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Did_you_know/Reviewing_guide" title="Wikipedia:Did you know/Reviewing guide">WP:Did you know/Reviewing guide</a>. </p>
      <p>To post a comment or review on a DYK nomination, follow the steps outlined below: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Look through this page, <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Template talk:Did you know</a>, to find a nomination you would like to comment on.</li> 
       <li>Click the "Review or comment" link at the top of the nomination. You will be taken to the nomination subpage.</li> 
       <li>The top of the page includes a list of the DYK criteria. Check the article to ensure it meets all the relevant criteria.</li> 
       <li>To indicate the result of the review (i.e., whether the nomination passes, fails, or needs some minor changes), leave a signed comment on the page. Please begin with one of the 5 review symbols that appear at the top of the edit screen, and then indicate all aspects of the article that you have reviewed; your comment should look something like the following:
        <blockquote>
         <p><code>Article length and age are fine, no copyvio or plagiarism concerns, reliable sources are used. But the hook needs to be shortened.</code></p>
        </blockquote> If you are the first person to comment on the nomination, there will be a line <code>:* &lt;!-- REPLACE THIS LINE TO WRITE FIRST COMMENT, KEEPING &nbsp;:* --&gt;</code> showing you where you should put the comment.</li> 
       <li>Save the page.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>If there is any problem or concern about a nomination, please consider notifying the nominator by placing <b>{{subst:DYKproblem|Article|header=yes|sig=yes}}</b> on the nominator's talk page. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Frequently_asked_questions">Frequently asked questions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template:DYK_nomination_header&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-4" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span id="Backlogged.3F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Backlogged?">Backlogged?</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template:DYK_nomination_header&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-5" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>This page is often backlogged. As long as your submission is still on the page, it will stay there until an editor reviews it. Since editors are encouraged to review the oldest submissions first (so that those hooks don't grow stale), it may take several weeks until your submission is reviewed. In the meantime, please consider reviewing another submission (not your own) to help reduce the backlog (see instructions above). </p> 
      <h4><span id="Where_is_my_hook.3F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Where_is_my_hook?">Where is my hook?</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template:DYK_nomination_header&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-6" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>If you can't find the nomination you submitted to <a class="mw-selflink selflink">this nominations</a> page, it may have been approved and is on the <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved" title="Template talk:Did you know/Approved">approved nominations</a> page waiting to be promoted. It could also have been added to one of the <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know/Queue#Prep_areas" title="Template:Did you know/Queue">prep areas</a>, promoted from prep to a <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know/Queue#Queues" title="Template:Did you know/Queue">queue</a>, or is on the main page. </p>
      <p>If the nominated hook is in none of those places, then the nomination has probably been rejected. Such a rejection usually only occurs if it was at least a couple of weeks old and had unresolved issues for which any discussion had gone stale. If you think your nomination was unfairly rejected, you can query this on the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia_talk:DYK" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia talk:DYK">DYK discussion page</a>, but as a general rule such nominations will only be restored in exceptional circumstances. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Search_archived_DYK_nomination_discussions">Search archived DYK nomination discussions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template:DYK_nomination_header&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-7" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

        <input type="hidden" value="Search" name="fulltext">
       </form>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Instructions_for_other_editors">Instructions for other editors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template:DYK_nomination_header&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-8" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="How_to_promote_an_accepted_hook">How to promote an accepted hook</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template:DYK_nomination_header&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-9" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li>See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Did_you_know/Preparation_areas" title="Wikipedia:Did you know/Preparation areas">Wikipedia:Did you know/Preparation areas</a> for full instructions.</li> 
       <li>Hooks that have been approved are located on the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:DYKNA" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:DYKNA">approved nominations page</a>.</li> 
       <li>In one window, open the DYK nomination subpage of the hook you would like to promote.</li> 
       <li>In another window, open the <b><a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know/Queue#Prep_areas" title="Template:Did you know/Queue">prep set</a></b> you intend to add the hook to.</li> 
       <li>In the prep set... 
        <ul>
         <li>Paste the hook into the hook area (be sure to not paste in <i>that that</i>)</li> 
         <li>Paste the credit information (<span class="nowrap">{{DYKmake}}</span> and/or <span class="nowrap">{{DYKnom}}</span>) into the credits area.</li> 
         <li>Add an edit summary, e.g. "Promoted [[Jane Fonda]]", preview, and save</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li>Back on DYK nomination page... 
        <ul>
         <li>change <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code>{{DYKsubpage</code></span> to <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code>{{<b>subst:</b>DYKsubpage</code></span></li> 
         <li>change <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code class="nowrap" style="">|passed=</code></span> to <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code class="nowrap" style="">|passed=yes</code></span></li> 
         <li>Add an edit summary, e.g. "Promoted to Prep 3", preview, and save</li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="How_to_remove_a_rejected_hook">How to remove a rejected hook</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template:DYK_nomination_header&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-10" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li>Open the DYK nomination subpage of the hook you would like to remove. (It's best to wait several days after a reviewer has rejected the hook, just in case someone contests or the article undergoes a large change.)</li> 
       <li>In the window where the DYK nomination subpage is open, replace the line <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code>{{DYKsubpage</code></span> with <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code>{{<b>subst:</b>DYKsubpage</code></span>, and replace <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code class="nowrap" style="">|passed=</code></span> with <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code class="nowrap" style="">|passed=no</code></span>. Then save the page. This has the effect of wrapping up the discussion on the DYK nomination subpage in a blue archive box and stating that the nomination was unsuccessful, as well as adding the nomination to a category for archival purposes.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="How_to_remove_a_hook_from_the_prep_areas_or_queue">How to remove a hook from the prep areas or queue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template:DYK_nomination_header&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-11" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li>Edit the prep area or queue where the hook is and remove the hook and the credits associated with it.</li> 
       <li>Go to the hook's nomination subpage (there should have been a link to it in the credits section). 
        <ul>
         <li>View the edit history for that page</li> 
         <li>Go back to the last version <i>before</i> the edit where the hook was promoted, and revert to that version to make the nomination active again.</li> 
         <li>Add a new icon on the nomination subpage to cancel the previous tick and leave a comment after it explaining that the hook was removed from the prep area or queue, and why, so that later reviewers are aware of this issue.</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li>Add a transclusion of the template back to this page so that reviewers can see it. It goes under the date that it was first created/expanded/listed as a GA. You may need to add back the day header for that date if it had been removed from this page.</li> 
       <li>If you removed the hook from a queue, it is best to either replace it with another hook from one of the prep areas, or to leave a message at <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia_talk:DYK" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia talk:DYK">WT:DYK</a> asking someone else to do so.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="How_to_move_a_nomination_subpage_to_a_new_name">How to move a nomination subpage to a new name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template:DYK_nomination_header&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-12" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li>Don't; it should not ever be necessary, and will break some links which will later need to be repaired. Even if you change the title of the article, you don't need to move the nomination page.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h1><span class="mw-headline" id="Nominations">Nominations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Nominations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h1> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Older_nominations">Older nominations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Older nominations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_February_17"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_February_17">Articles created/expanded on February 17</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on February 17">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span id="Koo_.28social_network.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Koo_(social_network)">Koo (social network)</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FKoo_App&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Koo_%28social_network%29&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Koo_(social_network)" title="Koo (social network)">Koo App</a></b> shot to prominence after Twitter got into a <a href="/wiki/2020%E2%80%932021_Indian_farmers%27_protest#social_media" title="2020–2021 Indian farmers' protest">weeks-long standoff</a> with the government of India? <small>Source:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.japantimes.co.jp/news/2021/02/17/business/koo-india-twitter/">Japan Times article</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that ...? <small>Source: "You are strongly encouraged to quote the source text supporting each hook" (and [link] the source, or cite it briefly without using citation templates)</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

           <table class="mw-collapsible mw-collapsed" border="1" style="border-collapse:collapse;"> 
            <tbody>
             <tr> 
              <th style="font-weight:normal;"><b>General:</b> Article is new enough and long enough </th>
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td> 
               <ul>
                <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Did_you_know#New" title="Wikipedia:Did you know">New Enough</a>: <img alt="Green tick" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/13px-Green_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/20px-Green_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/26px-Green_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"><span style="display:none">Y</span></li>

       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">Adequate sourcing</a>: <img alt="Red X" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Red_x.svg/13px-Red_x.svg.png" decoding="async" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Red_x.svg/20px-Red_x.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Red_x.svg/26px-Red_x.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"><span style="display: none;">N</span> - need sources for "first launched in Kannada", "Hindi", and all of the future languages. The Japan Times source says that Koo installs increased by 901,000, not that there were 901,000 installs</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NPOV" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NPOV">Neutral</a>: <img alt="Green tick" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/13px-Green_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/20px-Green_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/26px-Green_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"><span style="display:none">Y</span></li>

(FWIW, I think I agree that it should be moved since the name of the app is just "Koo")</li>

Reference [7] says: 
          <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r989825325">.mw-parser-output .inline-quote-talk{font-family:Georgia,"DejaVu Serif",serif;color:#008560;quotes:none}.mw-parser-output .inline-quote-talk-italic{font-family:inherit;font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output .inline-quote-talk-marks{quotes:"\"""\""}</style><q class="inline-quote-talk">It is named just “Koo” on the App Store with Bombinate Technologies Private Limited as the provider.</q> I think it's similar to how we have articles titled <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Snapchat" title="Snapchat">Snapchat</a> rather than "Twitter App" and "Snapchat App". Also, "first launched in Kannada", "Hindi", and all of the future languages should be sourced — I'm being annoying about this because if the unsourced material is removed it starts to approach the 1,500-character minimum DYK threshold. Thanks, let me know if you have any questions or if you want me to open it up for more opinions from <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia_talk:DYK" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia talk:DYK">WT:DYK</a>. <a href="/wiki/User:DanCherek" title="User:DanCherek">DanCherek</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:DanCherek" title="User talk:DanCherek">talk</a>) 20:14, 15 April 2021 (UTC)

            The prose is generally fine and GOCE is probably not necessary; DYK-compliant sourcing is the only thing preventing this from being approved right now. <a href="/wiki/User:DanCherek" title="User:DanCherek">DanCherek</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:DanCherek" title="User talk:DanCherek">talk</a>) 14:13, 30 May 2021 (UTC) 
            <dl>
             <dd>
              After all the recent edits to the article, I don't see any serious issue with the article right now. <b><a href="/wiki/User:Aman.kumar.goel" title="User:Aman.kumar.goel">Aman Kumar Goel</a></b> <sup>(<i><a href="/wiki/User_talk:Aman.kumar.goel" title="User talk:Aman.kumar.goel">Talk</a></i>)</sup> 10:56, 1 June 2021 (UTC)

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_March_18"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_March_18">Articles created/expanded on March 18</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on March 18">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuilin_Zhang">Cuilin Zhang</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FCuilin_Zhang&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cuilin_Zhang&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 128px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Cuilin_Zhang.jpg" class="image" title="Cuilin Zhang"><img alt="Cuilin Zhang" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Cuilin_Zhang.jpg/128px-Cuilin_Zhang.jpg" decoding="async" width="128" height="154" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Cuilin_Zhang.jpg/192px-Cuilin_Zhang.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Cuilin_Zhang.jpg/256px-Cuilin_Zhang.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="482"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Cuilin Zhang
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Cuilin_Zhang" title="Cuilin Zhang">Cuilin Zhang</a></b><span class="nowrap">'s</span> <i>(pictured)</i> research suggested that potatoes might increase the risk of <a href="/wiki/Gestational_diabetes" title="Gestational diabetes">gestational diabetes</a>? <small>Source: "Cuilin Zhang, lead study author, from the National Institutes of Health in Maryland, US, said the findings were important" "Potato-rich diet 'may increase pregnancy diabetes risk" <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.bbc.com/news/health-35261184">[1]</a><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.cbsnews.com/news/potatoes-pregnancy-gestational-diabetes-risk/">[2]</a></small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Jacquie_Sturm" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Jacquie Sturm">Template:Did you know nominations/Jacquie Sturm</a></li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: Public domain text used and identified in the article.</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p><small>Created by <a href="/wiki/User:TJMSmith" title="User:TJMSmith">TJMSmith</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:TJMSmith" title="User talk:TJMSmith">talk</a>). Self-nominated at 03:00, 18 March 2021 (UTC).</small> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_possible_vote.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol possible vote.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Symbol_possible_vote.svg/16px-Symbol_possible_vote.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Symbol_possible_vote.svg/24px-Symbol_possible_vote.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Symbol_possible_vote.svg/32px-Symbol_possible_vote.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> <span class="template-ping">@<a href="/wiki/User:TJMSmith" title="User:TJMSmith">TJMSmith</a>:</span> Most of the article is taken from a public domain source <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://irp.nih.gov/pi/cuilin-zhang">[3]</a>. This is allowed, but this text dcount towards the 1500 character requirement. I only count about 1100 characters of new text, so it needs a little more expansion.</li>
        </ul> 
        <dl>
         <dd>
          There are also sourcing issues. The non-copied text of the article is also entirely based on sources that aren't independent, so there really needs to be more text based on independent sources, preferably more than half the article. The copied text does have some added independent references, but they are popular media articles and one needs to be careful since these aren't considered reliable for biomedical statements (see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:MEDRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:MEDRS">WP:MEDRS</a>). <a href="/wiki/User:Antony-22" title="User:Antony-22">Antony–<i><b>22</b></i></a> (<sup><a href="/wiki/User_talk:Antony-22" title="User talk:Antony-22">talk</a></sup>?<sub><a href="/wiki/Special:Contributions/Antony-22" title="Special:Contributions/Antony-22">contribs</a></sub>) 06:53, 28 March 2021 (UTC) 
          <dl>
           <dd>
            <a href="/wiki/User:Antony-22" title="User:Antony-22">Antony-22</a>, I wasn't aware that the text doesn't count towards the 1500 requirement. Is that policy stated anywhere? I agree it would be preferable for there to be more independent sources. Academics are not always covered as frequently as other notable figures (like entertainers and athletes). I'm not sure if that this point alone disqualifies a DYK nomination. The majority of the content of this article is cites a reliable (but not independent) source. Thanks for the review! <a href="/wiki/User:TJMSmith" title="User:TJMSmith">TJMSmith</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:TJMSmith" title="User talk:TJMSmith">talk</a>) 14:24, 9 April 2021 (UTC) 
            <dl>
             <dd>
              It's part of <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:DYK#Eligibility_criteria" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:DYK">Rule 2b</a>. You can still add text or rewrite the PD text to satisfy the length requirement.
             </dd> 
             <dd>
              Generally these kinds of institutional biographies are "reliable" in the sense of being factual, and they can be used as sources, but they shouldn't be most or all of the citations. It's as much a neutrality issue as a verifiability one. Academics are sometime tricky to find independent sources for, but sometimes you can find news/perspectives articles like this one <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://jamanetwork.com/journals/jama/article-abstract/1878715">[4]</a>, or a piece in an alumni magazine or hometown newsletter, or even other journal articles that talk about their work. So how about this, do a search and see what you can come up with, and if there really isn't anything out there I'll say it's good enough since the article's only making straightforward factual statements anyway. <a href="/wiki/User:Antony-22" title="User:Antony-22">Antony–<i><b>22</b></i></a> (<sup><a href="/wiki/User_talk:Antony-22" title="User talk:Antony-22">talk</a></sup>?<sub><a href="/wiki/Special:Contributions/Antony-22" title="Special:Contributions/Antony-22">contribs</a></sub>) 21:40, 11 April 2021 (UTC) 
              <dl>
               <dd>

I wanted to acknowledge that I've read your response and will work on this Zhang article as soon as I can. I think I should have some time between now and 4/19. <a href="/wiki/User:TJMSmith" title="User:TJMSmith">TJMSmith</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:TJMSmith" title="User talk:TJMSmith">talk</a>) 02:04, 15 April 2021 (UTC)

         <li><b>ALT1:</b> ... that <b><a href="/wiki/Cuilin_Zhang" title="Cuilin Zhang">Cuilin Zhang</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> leads a study of about 4,000 women who had diabetes in pregnancy to identify factors in the progression from <a href="/wiki/Gestational_diabetes" title="Gestational diabetes">gestational diabetes</a> to <a href="/wiki/Type_2_diabetes" title="Type 2 diabetes">type 2 diabetes</a>? <small>Source: "Dr. Cuilin Zhang serves as the Principal Investigator of the Diabetes and Women's Health Study, which is a retrospective cohort study of approximately 4,000 women from U.S. and Denmark who had diabetes in pregnancy and have been followed up for at least 10 years. These women will be prospectively followed up for an additional four years to collect updated information on major environmental factors and timed biospecimens. The study is focusing on the identification of determinants (medical, lifestyle, genetic and their interactions) for the progression from gestational diabetes to type 2 diabetes and its complications and the investigation of biochemical markers that may predict the development of these complications among the pre-diabetic population." <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://irp.nih.gov/pi/cuilin-zhang">(public domain source)</a></small></li>

      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FSusana_Bloch&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

      <ul>
       <li><s>... that actors have been the first to benefit from <a href="/wiki/Experimental_psychology" title="Experimental psychology">experimental psychologist</a> <b><a href="/wiki/Susana_Bloch" title="Susana Bloch">Susana Bloch</a></b><span class="nowrap">'s</span> Alba Emoting method, allowing them to induce any of six <a href="/wiki/Basic_emotions" class="mw-redirect" title="Basic emotions">basic emotions</a> (sadness, joy, anger, fear, sexuality and tenderness) <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/32212066/">"using specific respiratory, postural, and facial behaviors"</a> then safely step out of them? </s> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:<s>... that <a href="/wiki/Experimental_psychology" title="Experimental psychology">experimental psychologist</a> <b><a href="/wiki/Susana_Bloch" title="Susana Bloch">Susana Bloch</a></b> has been teaching <a href="/wiki/Actor" title="Actor">actors</a> how to physically induce any of six genuine <a href="/wiki/Basic_emotions" class="mw-redirect" title="Basic emotions">emotions</a> (sadness, joy, anger, fear, sexuality and tenderness) by <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/32212066/">"using specific respiratory, postural, and facial behaviors"</a> as well as safely step out of them?</s></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

        Welcome to DYK, <a href="/wiki/User:Remando" title="User:Remando">Remando</a>! I haven't looked at the article yet, for lack of time, but just some hopefully helpful hints: 
        <ul>
         <li>You can bold "outside" the brackets of links which makes it easier, - done for you here.</li> 
         <li>In such cases, an apostrophe needs a template, - done for you.</li> 
         <li>The hooks are too long, not only formally, - they also tell too much. You want to make people get curious, not give the :impression they know it all when reading the hook.</li> 
         <li>External links - like to the book - are a no-no, not only in hooks, also in article prose.</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>

I'll watch, and possibly review when I have time. --<a href="/wiki/User:Gerda_Arendt" title="User:Gerda Arendt">Gerda Arendt</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Gerda_Arendt" title="User talk:Gerda Arendt">talk</a>) 09:44, 23 April 2021 (UTC)

           <dd>
            <a href="/wiki/User:Remando" title="User:Remando">Remando</a>, thank you for the offers, with good ideas, but none ready to be approved. They'd all need "... that" at the beginning. I don't think hiding her gender is a good idea, and therefore suggest to give her her name. My simple idea for a hook would be just repeat what the lead says. - Some concerns in the article: 
            <ul>
             <li>I'm not sure about Professor vs. professor, and Psychology vs. psychology. Please go over that, leaving only titles capital.</li> 
             <li>Why not use the lovely image here?</li> 
             <li>The grammar of "modulate basic emotions using the body and particular breathing patterns" - somehow doesn't work for me.</li> 
             <li>She is very cautious about no birth year, but can anything please have a year, like graduation, move to France, whatever?</li> 
             <li>I'm particularly curious where Arendt comes from</li> 
             <li>Please avoid constructions such as "It was there she and ..." and "It was this collaboration ...".</li> 
             <li>Please avoid - generally - to have a full date in md-format as an adjective, as for the <a href="/wiki/1973_Chilean_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1973 Chilean coup d'état">Chilean coup d'état</a>. I fixed it here.</li> 
             <li>Check for repetition of "working".</li> 
             <li>"where she continues to devote her time to teaching, developing new practical applications in various areas and internationally, and writing about her work" - that doesn't need any "devotion of time", and is unclear where "and internationally" connects to.</li> 
             <li>I had no idea that "sexuality" and "tenderness" are emotions, - does that come from translation?</li> 
             <li>"genuine, organic emotion" - what's that?</li> 
             <li>Books and Awards need references.</li> 
             <li>I wonder if some detail from the references should be quoted in the article, because going back and forth is tricky.</li>
            </ul>
           </dd> 
           <dd>
            <a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_question.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol question.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/16px-Symbol_question.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/24px-Symbol_question.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/32px-Symbol_question.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> Interesting research, on fine sources, offline sources accepted AGF, no copyvio obvious.                    <dd>
                    It's one fact: the Duke chose someone who was more or less unknown, composing and playing guitar and singing/writing Pop songs, for writing that piece of church music for his birthdays and other functions at Windsor Castle. More elegant wording welcome, but don't don't tell me that's two facts, please. The fact of writing a cantata on a psalm without that contrast is boring, imho. --<a href="/wiki/User:Gerda_Arendt" title="User:Gerda Arendt">Gerda Arendt</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Gerda_Arendt" title="User talk:Gerda Arendt">talk</a>) 11:36, 30 May 2021 (UTC) 
                    <dl>
                     <dd>
                      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r989825325"><q class="inline-quote-talk">The fact of writing a cantata on a psalm without that contrast is boring, imho.</q> - the hook isn't for you, though, and how many people reading DYK do you actually expect even know what a cantata <i>is</i>, let alone how it relates to a psalm and how that relates to guitar music. Do you think it will be boring to other people? (And it is two facts because of how you're using active voice to say Lovelady composed guitar music - there are passive ways of establishing the difference, like in my suggestion above - and because they can be read separately and aren't explicitly connected - people with processing disorders or even just those a little slow at comprehension aren't going to see how the parts relate.) It is interesting that a pop guitar composer did some church music, and that Prince Philip requested someone relatively unknown, but putting it all in one hook won't be that easy. <a href="/wiki/User:Kingsif" title="User:Kingsif">Kingsif</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Kingsif" title="User talk:Kingsif">talk</a>) 12:17, 30 May 2021 (UTC)

                       <dd>
                        <dl>
                         <dd>
                          Personally I thought the Prince Philip angle was always the more hooky part and the one that would raise the most interest. There's nothing wrong with mentioning Incantations and there are several ways to include that in the hook, but as Kingsif said it's too clunky to try to juggle two different hook facts at the same time, plus the nuance of him being obscure is difficult to mention anyway. <a href="/wiki/User:Narutolovehinata5" title="User:Narutolovehinata5">Narutolovehinata5</a> <sup><a href="/wiki/User_talk:Narutolovehinata5" title="User talk:Narutolovehinata5">t</a><a href="/wiki/Special:Contributions/Narutolovehinata5" title="Special:Contributions/Narutolovehinata5">c</a><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:CSD" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:CSD">csd</a><a href="/wiki/Special:NewPages" title="Special:NewPages">new</a></sup> 12:42, 30 May 2021 (UTC)

                       <dd>
                        You know that English is not my native tongue, and I hope you know that I tried. I was taught that active voice is better than passive, - do you tell me otherwise? <i><a href="/wiki/Incantation" title="Incantation">Incantations</a></i> has an "obscure" / "ancient rites" connatations, - do you tell me that's wrong. We can drop cantata. (But after more than 100 hooks about Bach cantatas, a regular DYK reader will know what a cantata is). People interested will likely have followed the funeral, and may remember that it was sung, and cantata means just "chanted music". <i>I</i> wanted to know who that Mr. Lovelady was, and the hook tries to give an answer. (I didn't watch it, but as <a href="/wiki/Schm%C3%BCcke_dich,_o_liebe_Seele" title="Schmücke dich, o liebe Seele">Schmücke dich, o liebe Seele</a> was mentioned on my talk I became interested in the two pieces commissioned for joyful celebrations (which a hook says about the other piece, please don't suggest to repeat that), and listened to those. --<a href="/wiki/User:Gerda_Arendt" title="User:Gerda Arendt">Gerda Arendt</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Gerda_Arendt" title="User talk:Gerda Arendt">talk</a>) 15:49, 1 June 2021 (UTC) 
                        <dl>
                         <dd>
                          Whether or not a hook is active or passive doesn't matter too much, what matters is how it flows. While the active voice is usually preferred, some hooks work better passive. It really depends on the circumstances and we don't have strict rules about it. <a href="/wiki/User:Narutolovehinata5" title="User:Narutolovehinata5">Narutolovehinata5</a> <sup><a href="/wiki/User_talk:Narutolovehinata5" title="User talk:Narutolovehinata5">t</a><a href="/wiki/Special:Contributions/Narutolovehinata5" title="Special:Contributions/Narutolovehinata5">c</a><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:CSD" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:CSD">csd</a><a href="/wiki/Special:NewPages" title="Special:NewPages">new</a></sup> 01:48, 2 June 2021 (UTC)
                         </dd>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Jane_Margyl">Jane Margyl</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FJane_Margyl&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Jane_Margyl&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 118px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Margyl1905_(cropped).JPG" class="image" title="Jane Margyl as Dalila"><img alt="Jane Margyl as Dalila" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Margyl1905_%28cropped%29.JPG/118px-Margyl1905_%28cropped%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="118" height="166" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Margyl1905_%28cropped%29.JPG/177px-Margyl1905_%28cropped%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Margyl1905_%28cropped%29.JPG/236px-Margyl1905_%28cropped%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1435" data-file-height="2016"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Jane Margyl as Dalila
        </div>

      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Jane_Margyl" title="Jane Margyl">Jane Margyl</a></b>, who was a celebrated star at the <a href="/wiki/Folies_Berg%C3%A8re" title="Folies Bergère">Folies Bergère</a>, became a <a href="/wiki/Mezzo-soprano" title="Mezzo-soprano">mezzo-soprano</a> appearing as <a href="/wiki/Samson_and_Delilah_(opera)" title="Samson and Delilah (opera)">Dalila</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Opera" title="Paris Opera">Paris Opera</a> in 1905 <i>(pictured)</i>? <small>Source: several</small></li>
      </ul>

And, and this is bigger, the citations aren't correct: "Gallica" is not the publisher. The hook is verified to an article from <i>Le monde artiste</i>, and it's titled "Courrier de la semaine", on p. 621--all that information needs to be in the citation, and it's the same for almost all the other citations. <a href="/wiki/User:Drmies" title="User:Drmies">Drmies</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Drmies" title="User talk:Drmies">talk</a>) 17:06, 5 May 2021 (UTC)

       <dd>
        I just spent ten minutes on the first sentence of the "Life" section, making copy edits (punctuation), completing the templates (page numbers, authors), and checking the facts. Looking at other references I see that more of the same needs to be done, and it seems to me that there are a lot of minor edits to be made as well. A few examples: L'Enlèvement des Sabines should probably link to <a href="/wiki/The_Rape_of_the_Sabine_Women" title="The Rape of the Sabine Women">The Rape of the Sabine Women</a>, because our audience is mostly English readers. The xs4all website is not reliable unless a strong case can be made for it, but I looked at the index and I am not sure how (it's someone's hobby project--admirable, but I don't think it will stand up to strong scrutiny). The "Family" section lists at least one person with no claim to notability, and a <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://gillesdubois.blogspot.com/2009/08/jane-margyl-et-georgette-sandry-de-la.html">questionable link</a> to a blog of someone who scours cemeteries. Best to cut that name, but then the text needs to be adjusted too... <a href="/wiki/User:Drmies" title="User:Drmies">Drmies</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Drmies" title="User talk:Drmies">talk</a>) 19:52, 20 May 2021 (UTC)
       </dd>

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_May_1"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_May_1">Articles created/expanded on May 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on May 1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Frederick_Strange">Frederick Strange</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FFrederick_Strange&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Frederick_Strange&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 120px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Frederick_Strange.png" class="image" title="Frederick Strange"><img alt="Frederick Strange" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Frederick_Strange.png/120px-Frederick_Strange.png" decoding="async" width="120" height="164" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Frederick_Strange.png/180px-Frederick_Strange.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Frederick_Strange.png/240px-Frederick_Strange.png 2x" data-file-width="994" data-file-height="1358"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word; text-align: center;">
         Frederick Strange
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li><s>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Strange" title="Frederick Strange">Frederick Strange</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> sought to replace John Gilbert as the premier natural history collector in the new Australian colonies, then met a similar fate?</s> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>: <s>... that an expedition by plant and animal collector <b><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Strange" title="Frederick Strange">Frederick Strange</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> resulted in the deaths of twelve people?</s></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li class="mw-empty-elt"></li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: I went to stub this and link around to the taxa Strange had something to with—it's only tangentially related to my supposed focus—,but some spontaneous collaboration produced a short but interesting article with rich referencing [cheers again for <span class="template-ping">@<a href="/wiki/User:Oronsay" title="User:Oronsay">Oronsay</a>:</span> contribs]. The flaws are mine, and I haven't checked length or other criteria since my last nom, but there is a potential dyk here and I or any one else willing can get it ship-shape. P.S. I added an image, but that parameter has been sucked away by a bot?</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Stephan_Hanna_Stephan">Stephan Hanna Stephan</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FStephan_Hanna_Stephan&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Stephan_Hanna_Stephan&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li><s>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Stephan_Hanna_Stephan" title="Stephan Hanna Stephan">Stephan Hanna Stephan</a></b> wrote about Palestinian folk songs and the Song of songs?</s> <small>Source: "The earliest of Stephan's works, "The Palestinian Parallels to the Song of Songs" (1922) documented the lyrics of folk songs in Palestine and compared them to biblical, Mesopotamian and <a href="/wiki/Canaanite" class="mw-disambig" title="Canaanite">Canaanite</a> precursors."<sup id="cite_ref-Irving2017p42_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irving2017p42-1">[1]</a></sup></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><s><b>ALT1</b>:... that the Mandate Palestine Government radio station had an 'Arab Hour' that was hosted by Palestinian writers like <b><a href="/wiki/Stephan_Hanna_Stephan" title="Stephan Hanna Stephan">Stephan Hanna Stephan</a></b>?</s><small>Source: "Beginning in 1936, Stephan was also a broadcaster on the Mandatory Government radio station's <i>Arab Hour</i>, where he shared much of his interest in ethnography and history with the Arabic speaking population of Palestine."<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <ul>
           <li><b>ALT1.0</b>:... that the radio station in Mandatory Palestine had an 'Arab Hour' in the late 1930s hosting Palestinian writers like <b><a href="/wiki/Stephan_Hanna_Stephan" title="Stephan Hanna Stephan">Stephan Hanna Stephan</a></b>? <small>Source: "Beginning in 1936, Stephan was also a broadcaster on the Mandatory Government radio station's <i>Arab Hour</i>, where he shared much of his interest in ethnography and history with the Arabic speaking population of Palestine."<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></small></li>
          </ul>
         </dd>
        </dl>
       </dd>
      </dl>

       <dd>

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_May_2"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_May_2">Articles created/expanded on May 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on May 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Norman_K._Risjord">Norman K. Risjord</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FNorman_K._Risjord&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Norman_K._Risjord&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that historian <b><a href="/wiki/Norman_K._Risjord" title="Norman K. Risjord">Norman K. Risjord</a></b> worked in counter-intelligence in Berlin before he obtained his Phd and pursued a career in American history?&nbsp;&nbsp;<small>Sources:&nbsp;• Norman K. Risjord: University of Wisconsin, biography; &nbsp;&nbsp;• Memorials: Norman Risjord, Omohundro Institute</small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Kammermusik_(Hindemith)" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Kammermusik (Hindemith)">Template:Did you know nominations/Kammermusik (Hindemith)</a></li>

        </ul>

      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_question.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol question.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/16px-Symbol_question.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/24px-Symbol_question.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/32px-Symbol_question.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> I am willing to review it, but first, the subject's <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:N" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:N">notability</a> is not clear. Could you elaborate here or on the article's talk how they meet <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NPROF" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NPROF">WP:NPROF</a>/<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NBIO" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NBIO">WP:NBIO</a> and ping me? The current sources for the article are low-key obituaries from his Department and funeral home, hardly independent (one presumably written by his colleagues at work, the other by his family and friends). I'll continue the review once the notability is made clear. --<sub style="border:1px solid #228B22;padding:1px;"><a href="/wiki/User:Piotrus" title="User:Piotrus">Piotr Konieczny aka Prokonsul Piotrus</a>|<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Piotrus" title="User talk:Piotrus"><span style="color:#7CFC00;background:#006400;"> reply here</span></a></sub> 07:37, 27 May 2021 (UTC)</li>

            <span class="template-ping">@<a href="/wiki/User:Piotrus" title="User:Piotrus">Piotrus</a>:</span> -- Risjord is noted in the academic and historical community for having authored more than twenty books on American history. That he worked for US intelligence before pursuing a career in history also makes him interesting, imo. The article is for reference, as Risjord's name occurs from time to time in other works of history. I wouldn't go so far as to say he's <i>famous</i>, but he is noted among historians and the like. -- <a href="/wiki/User:Gwillhickers" title="User:Gwillhickers"><i>Gwillhickers</i></a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Gwillhickers" title="User talk:Gwillhickers">talk</a>) 23:01, 3 June 2021 (UTC)

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_May_4"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_May_4">Articles created/expanded on May 4</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on May 4">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Bomber_Mafia">The Bomber Mafia</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FThe_Bomber_Mafia&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=The_Bomber_Mafia&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Gladwell" title="Malcolm Gladwell">Malcolm Gladwell</a> devoted four episodes of his podcast <i><a href="/wiki/Revisionist_History_(podcast)" title="Revisionist History (podcast)">Revisionist History</a></i> to air power in World War II before writing <i><b><a href="/wiki/The_Bomber_Mafia" title="The Bomber Mafia">The Bomber Mafia</a></b></i>? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://podcasts.google.com/feed/aHR0cHM6Ly9mZWVkcy5tZWdhcGhvbmUuZm0vcmV2aXNpb25pc3RoaXN0b3J5/episode/YjQ0OWFmOTYtYTM3MS0xMWViLWI5NzgtM2YwOWY5MDE5YmUz?sa=X&amp;ved=0CAUQkfYCahcKEwiApK_zirHwAhUAAAAAHQAAAAAQGQ">[5]</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that <a href="/wiki/Thomas_E._Ricks_(journalist)" title="Thomas E. Ricks (journalist)">Thomas E. Ricks</a> called <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Gladwell" title="Malcolm Gladwell">Malcolm Gladwell</a>'s <i><b><a href="/wiki/The_Bomber_Mafia" title="The Bomber Mafia">The Bomber Mafia</a></b></i> "a conversational work"? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/25/books/review/the-bomber-mafia-malcolm-gladwell.html">[6]</a></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Gladwell" title="Malcolm Gladwell">Malcolm Gladwell</a>'s <i><b><a href="/wiki/The_Bomber_Mafia" title="The Bomber Mafia">The Bomber Mafia</a></b></i> began as an audiobook before it transitioned to a print book? <small>Source: Gladwell 2021, p. 209</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT3</b>:... that military historian <a href="/wiki/Saul_David" title="Saul David">Saul David</a> called <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Gladwell" title="Malcolm Gladwell">Malcolm Gladwell</a>'s <i><b><a href="/wiki/The_Bomber_Mafia" title="The Bomber Mafia">The Bomber Mafia</a></b></i> "error prone" and "bedevilled by the same oversimplification of the world into a single Big Idea that is characteristic of his other work"? <small><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.telegraph.co.uk/books/what-to-read/malcolm-gladwells-bomber-mafia-misleading-history-lite/">1</a></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <p><b>Policy compliance:</b> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">Adequate sourcing</a>: <img alt="Red X" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Red_x.svg/13px-Red_x.svg.png" decoding="async" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Red_x.svg/20px-Red_x.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Red_x.svg/26px-Red_x.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"><span style="display: none;">N</span> - Does not meet inline citation requirements (the exception is fiction works can have plot that's verifiable to the original, but not nonfiction works). You can fix this by adding inline citations with page numbers in the book where the points are supported.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NPOV" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NPOV">Neutral</a>: <img alt="Green tick" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/13px-Green_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/20px-Green_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/26px-Green_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"><span style="display:none">Y</span></li> 
       <li>Free of <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Copyright_violations" title="Wikipedia:Copyright violations">copyright violations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Plagiarism" title="Wikipedia:Plagiarism">plagiarism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Close_paraphrasing" title="Wikipedia:Close paraphrasing">close paraphrasing</a>: <img alt="Green tick" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/13px-Green_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/20px-Green_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/26px-Green_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"><span style="display:none">Y</span></li>
      </ul> 
      <p><b>Hook eligibility:</b> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Did_you_know#Cited_hook" title="Wikipedia:Did you know">Cited</a>: <img alt="Green tick" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/13px-Green_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/20px-Green_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/26px-Green_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"><span style="display:none">Y</span> - Offline/paywalled citation accepted in good faith</li> 
       <li>Interesting: <img alt="Red X" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Red_x.svg/13px-Red_x.svg.png" decoding="async" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Red_x.svg/20px-Red_x.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Red_x.svg/26px-Red_x.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"><span style="display: none;">N</span> - I don't really see how either of the hooks is that interesting. "Conversational" is typical for popular history works. It's not surprising that he would discuss on his podcast and then publish a book</li>

      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FOlivos_and_Tezonco_stations&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a> )</li>

      <ul>
       <li>... that the Superior Audit Office of the Federation of Mexico made observations in 2017 of damages to the <b><a href="/wiki/Tezonco_metro_station" title="Tezonco metro station">Tezonco</a></b>–<b><a href="/wiki/Olivos_metro_station" title="Olivos metro station">Olivos</a></b> section <i>(pictured)</i> previous to <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Metro_overpass_collapse" title="Mexico City Metro overpass collapse">its collapse in May 2021</a>? <small>Source: "Justo en el tramo de las estaciones Olivos-Tezonco, la Auditoría Superior de la Federación, realizó algunas observaciones de daños luego del sismo ocurrido en septiembre del año 2017, mismos que no se resolvieron." ["Right in the Olivos-Tezonco stations section, the Superior Audit Office of the Federation, made some observations of damages after the earthquake occurred in September 2017, which were not resolved.]" (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://canal44.com/nacional/reportaron-errores-y-danos-antes-y-despues-del-sismo-de-la-linea-12-del-metro/">Canal 44</a>)</small></li>
      </ul>

I did have to improve both pages to make the writing more idiomatic, and the hook needs the same treatment. I'm particularly wondering if "Superior Auditor of the Federation" (which I had personally used in my work before) may be a better translation for the ASF, though I note that English-language published material is absolutely all over the place, for instance <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.oecd.org/governance/ethics/WEB_ASF%20Progress%20report%20ENGLISH.pdf">this OECD report</a> uses three different translations (and I'm contemplating writing the missing article).       <h4><span id="Sabacc.2C_Dejarik"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Sabacc,_Dejarik">Sabacc, Dejarik</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FSabacc&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( Article history links: <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sabacc&amp;action=history">Sabacc</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dejarik&amp;action=history">Dejarik</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that neither of the two Star Wars in-universe games, <b><a href="/wiki/Dejarik" title="Dejarik">dejarik</a></b> (aka holochess) and <b><a href="/wiki/Sabacc" title="Sabacc">sabacc</a></b>, have a single, definite and canon rule-set despite several real-world licensed releases? <small>Source: For d: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20200309204108/https://www.starwars.com/series/star-wars-rebels/always-two-there-are-trivia-gallery">"actual gameplay rules developed but never publicly released"</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://ca.games.yahoo.com/blogs/unplugged/fiction-most-famous-games-play-them-real-234912482.html">"there's at least one fan-made set of rules"</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=pAjYCgAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PT325&amp;redir_esc=y#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false">"no official licenced home version of holochess has yet been issued. However, fans have written rules for the game"</a>. Note that the first part of this sentence is no longer true. For s: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.dailydot.com/parsec/how-to-play-sabacc-solo-star-wars/">"Like the holographic strategy game Dejarik, Sabacc appears onscreen without an in-depth explanation of the rules...Various tie-in books and games have offered their own take on Sabacc... Within the new canon, you’ll find a semi-official (albeit simplified) version of those rules... If you want to play Sabacc yourself, Wookieepedia has a guide to the rules...We won’t be surprised if Disney releases a more canon-specific version of the game later on. But if the “official” rules turn out to be different from the ones you learned from Wookieepedia, don’t get sweat it"</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://screenrant.com/star-wars-sabacc-card-game-solo-rules-play/">"pecific rules can vary depending on who's playing"</a></small></li>
      </ul>

       <dd>

         <li><i>Comment</i>: This double-article nom superceeds my recent <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Dejarik" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Dejarik">Template:Did you know nominations/Dejarik</a> (where I linked the second QPQ) unless there is a good argument to have two separate hooks. Also, <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Day" title="Star Wars Day">Star Wars Day</a> is... today, if anyone wants to help speedying this up.</li>

      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>

       <li>... that adult film actress <b><a href="/wiki/Kendra_Sunderland" title="Kendra Sunderland">Kendra Sunderland</a></b> originally wanted to be a counselor or an accountant? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nydailynews.com/news/national/oregon-webcam-girl-kendra-sunderland-interview-article-1.2105248">New York Daily News</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that when <b><a href="/wiki/Kendra_Sunderland" title="Kendra Sunderland">Kendra Sunderland</a></b> won an award, <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> designed a t-shirt with her name and likeness on it? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.complex.com/style/2018/09/kanye-west-pornhub-awards-merch">Complex</a></small></li>
        </ul></li>

      <p><b>Overall</b>: <a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_question.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol question.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/16px-Symbol_question.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/24px-Symbol_question.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/32px-Symbol_question.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> Article is all good. But misses on timelines. Like it does not mention that she won the award in 2018. Also, there is no censorship required in the article (censorship <i>may</i> be required on main page). Hence you can freely mention the tits in the article but maybe skip from the hook. In fact, you can rephrase Alt1 in such an intriguing manner that people will want to click and read full article to know for what she won the award. §§<a href="/wiki/User:Dharmadhyaksha" title="User:Dharmadhyaksha"><i style="color:#E0115F"><b>Dharmadhyaksha</b></i></a>§§ <small>{<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Dharmadhyaksha" title="User talk:Dharmadhyaksha">Talk</a> / <a href="/wiki/Special:Contributions/Dharmadhyaksha" title="Special:Contributions/Dharmadhyaksha">Edits</a>}</small> 11:42, 11 May 2021 (UTC) </p>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Sweet_Flypaper_of_Life">The Sweet Flypaper of Life</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FThe_Sweet_Flypaper_of_Life&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

      <ul>
       <li>... that although the photographs in <i><b><a href="/wiki/The_Sweet_Flypaper_of_Life" title="The Sweet Flypaper of Life">The Sweet Flypaper of Life</a></b></i> were described as "unpublishable in book form", after <a href="/wiki/Langston_Hughes" title="Langston Hughes">Langston Hughes</a> wrote accompanying text it became a critical and commercial success?</li>
      </ul>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Toma_Kamijo">Toma Kamijo</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FToma_Kamijo&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

      <div class="plainlinks hlist">
