        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the black <a href="/wiki/Domino_mask" title="Domino mask">domino mask</a> in the&nbsp;<i><b><a href="/wiki/Portrait_of_a_Woman_with_Mask" title="Portrait of a Woman with Mask">Portrait of a Woman with Mask</a></b></i> <i>(pictured)</i> gives us a clue that the portrait was painted during the artist's own era? <small>Source: "The black domino she is holding in her right hand takes us back to the artist’s own era, in a subtle play of fiction and reality." <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.artgate-cariplo.it/collezione-online/page37d.do?link=oln94d.redirect&amp;kcond32d.att1=884&amp;scu5d.scroller.att78d=884">Fondazione Cariplo Artgate</a></small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/St._George%27s_Basilica,_Prague" title="Template:Did you know nominations/St. George's Basilica, Prague">St. George's Basilica, Prague</a></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>

      <p><small>Created by <a href="/wiki/User:JeBonSer" title="User:JeBonSer">JeBonSer</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:JeBonSer" title="User talk:JeBonSer">talk</a>). Self-nominated at 23:31, 23 May 2021 (UTC).</small> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_question.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol question.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/16px-Symbol_question.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/24px-Symbol_question.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/32px-Symbol_question.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> <a href="/wiki/User:JeBonSer" title="User:JeBonSer">JeBonSer</a>, that's an interesting painting, on few but good sources, no copyvio obvious. The image is licensed, and a DYK without it would miss the point. I find some things unusual in the article. I reduced overlinking myself, but please help me: 
        <ol>
         <li>The lead should be a summary! <s>Not details about dimensions.</s> Please have everything from the lead <i>also</i> in the body, with the ref in the body, and have only <i>important facts</i> in the lead.</li> 
         <li>The link to the current city of Venice is not helpful, - what we need is a link to the Venetian art of a former period, and best with a year or two. At present, what the hook claims is not even in the article: that her work looks like something earlier. Not every reader will be versed in art history enough to know without being told.</li> 
         <li>I believe that you could use the pdf for a reference.</li> 
         <li>I don't read Italian besides being able to order from a menu, so can't tell if the English ref is just a translation of the Italian, in which case we'd need only one.</li>
        </ol>
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        The hook has a bit of the same problem (as 2. above): as the painter is not named, an unprepared reader will not even see two periods in the pastel, at a glance at least. Best advice I can give: try an easier hook. The picture alone will attract, - it doesn't have to be super fancy. In article and hook, I'd like to see sooner that the creator was a woman, but that may be just me. I'd prefer her name in the hook rather than in the already long image caption. I will not approve a hook that says "us", - "we" and "us" don't belong in Wikipedia (unless in quotes). I removed a comma in the hook that broke the sentence. Please word a new hook below. --<a href="/wiki/User:Gerda_Arendt" title="User:Gerda Arendt">Gerda Arendt</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Gerda_Arendt" title="User talk:Gerda Arendt">talk</a>) 10:04, 25 May 2021 (UTC) 
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <b>Comment</b> Gerda, the lead is EXACTLY the right place to put dimensions! <a href="/wiki/Venetian_painting" title="Venetian painting">Venetian painting</a> could be linked, to the appropriate section. I agree the hook is odd. As usual with this nominator, the terrible English should be the first thing to mention " it is now currently displayed..." and so on. <a href="/wiki/User:JeBonSer" title="User:JeBonSer">User:JeBonSer</a>, "now" and "currently" <i>mean the same thing</i>. <a href="/wiki/User:Johnbod" title="User:Johnbod">Johnbod</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Johnbod" title="User talk:Johnbod">talk</a>) 16:55, 25 May 2021 (UTC) 
          <dl>
           <dd>
            Learning: For a piece of music, I wouldn't give duration and tempo markings in the lead, but the visual arts seem to be different. --<a href="/wiki/User:Gerda_Arendt" title="User:Gerda Arendt">Gerda Arendt</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Gerda_Arendt" title="User talk:Gerda Arendt">talk</a>) 17:10, 25 May 2021 (UTC)
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </dd> 
         <dd>
          <b>ALT1</b>: ... that the <i><b><a href="/wiki/Portrait_of_a_Woman_with_Mask" title="Portrait of a Woman with Mask">Portrait of a Woman with Mask</a></b></i> <i>(pictured)</i> by <a href="/wiki/Rosalba_Carriera" title="Rosalba Carriera">Rosalba Carriera</a> has no exact date when it was being painted, but through a label at the back of the portrait this gives help to its keepers to trace its origins? <small>Source: "Although the history of this pastel prior to its appearance on the antique market is unknown, its provenance from the Galleria Lorenzelli in Bergamo is documented by a label on the back of the work and by an estimate drawn up in Italian lire by Sotheby’s at an unspecified date, but presumably around 1999 since part of Intesa Leasing’s assets were sold to Iniziative Patrimoniali S.p.A. in the same year." <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.artgate-cariplo.it/collezione-online/page37d.do?link=oln94d.redirect&amp;kcond32d.att1=884&amp;scu5d.scroller.att78d=884">Fondazione Cariplo Artgate</a></small>
         </dd> 
         <dd>
          <span class="template-ping">@<a href="/wiki/User:Gerda_Arendt" title="User:Gerda Arendt">Gerda Arendt</a>:</span> 
          <img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/U2713.svg/18px-U2713.svg.png" decoding="async" width="18" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/U2713.svg/27px-U2713.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/U2713.svg/36px-U2713.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="325"> <b>Resolved</b>. <b><a href="/wiki/User:JeBonSer" title="User:JeBonSer"><span style="color:#00CED1">Je</span><span style="color:#007F94">Bon</span><span style="color:#4B0082"><i>Ser</i></span></a></b> <sup>(<a href="/wiki/User_talk:JeBonSer" title="User talk:JeBonSer">talk</a> | <a href="/wiki/User:JeBonSer/Guestbook" title="User:JeBonSer/Guestbook">sign</a>)</sup> 09:14, 31 May 2021 (UTC) 
          <dl>
           <dd>
            Thank you for offering a new hook, but I confess I find it wordy. Perhaps I should leave reviewing to a native speaker. "date when it was being painted" is long for nothing, "gives help" could be simpler, and why mention "keepers" at all? Actually, the same is true for the article, just look at "The extraordinary skill of Carriera in arts can be easily seen in the portrait including Venetian painter's influence of the 18th-century Venetian style of paintings that can be easily recognised on this portrait." - duplications and saying something such as "extraordinary skill" as if a fact. I'm afraid if the article is trimmed to a concise style - in this case drop repetition of "Venetian", and use less flowery language, it might be too short. Do you want to continue with me, or rather ask for a different reviewer". --<a href="/wiki/User:Gerda_Arendt" title="User:Gerda Arendt">Gerda Arendt</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Gerda_Arendt" title="User talk:Gerda Arendt">talk</a>) 10:45, 31 May 2021 (UTC) 
            <dl>
             <dd>
              It's up to you <a href="/wiki/User:Gerda_Arendt" title="User:Gerda Arendt">Gerda Arendt</a>. <b><a href="/wiki/User:JeBonSer" title="User:JeBonSer"><span style="color:#00CED1">Je</span><span style="color:#007F94">Bon</span><span style="color:#4B0082"><i>Ser</i></span></a></b> <sup>(<a href="/wiki/User_talk:JeBonSer" title="User talk:JeBonSer">talk</a> | <a href="/wiki/User:JeBonSer/Guestbook" title="User:JeBonSer/Guestbook">sign</a>)</sup> 11:27, 31 May 2021 (UTC) 
              <dl>
               <dd>
                <a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_redirect_vote_4.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol redirect vote 4.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Symbol_redirect_vote_4.svg/16px-Symbol_redirect_vote_4.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Symbol_redirect_vote_4.svg/24px-Symbol_redirect_vote_4.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Symbol_redirect_vote_4.svg/32px-Symbol_redirect_vote_4.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> Let's do it like this: you try to find someone less persistent, and if you can't find one, ping me, but not without substantial changes to the article prose, and a trimmed hook. --<a href="/wiki/User:Gerda_Arendt" title="User:Gerda Arendt">Gerda Arendt</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Gerda_Arendt" title="User talk:Gerda Arendt">talk</a>) 12:12, 31 May 2021 (UTC)

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="That_Bloody_Woman">That Bloody Woman</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FThat_Bloody_Woman&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=That_Bloody_Woman&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that Greg Cooper based the character of suffragist <a href="/wiki/Kate_Sheppard" title="Kate Sheppard">Kate Sheppard</a> in punk-rock musical <i><b><a href="/wiki/That_Bloody_Woman" title="That Bloody Woman">That Bloody Woman</a></b></i> on <a href="/wiki/Bette_Midler" title="Bette Midler">Bette Midler</a> in concert in Cleveland? <small>Source: "GC: I was talking to my partner, Sarah. I said I want Kate to be sexy and sassy and in control. Sarah said, 'a bit like Bette Midler'. And I said, 'My God, yes, exactly like Bette Midler'. We went on YouTube and found this incredible concert she did in 1977 in Cleveland." (Source <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.stuff.co.nz/entertainment/stage-and-theatre/82013535/that-bloody-struggle-the-making-of-hit-musical-that-bloody-woman">Stuff newspaper article</a> on writing of the musical)</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that when Luke Di Somma approached Gregory Cooper to co-write <i><b><a href="/wiki/That_Bloody_Woman" title="That Bloody Woman">That Bloody Woman</a></b></i>, Cooper had to Google the term "<a href="/wiki/Libretto" title="Libretto">librettist</a>"? <small>Source: "I emailed him and said I know we have only met once, but I have this idea and I think I might need a librettist. He wrote back and said I have Googled librettist and I think I can do it, let's talk." (Source <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.stuff.co.nz/entertainment/stage-and-theatre/82013535/that-bloody-struggle-the-making-of-hit-musical-that-bloody-woman">Stuff newspaper article</a> on writing of the musical)</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Robert_Louis_Stevenson_Museum" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Robert Louis Stevenson Museum">Robert Louis Stephenson Museum</a></li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: Am trying to source photo.</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Joe_Beckwith">Joe Beckwith</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FJoe_Beckwith&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Joe_Beckwith&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 116px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Joe_Beckwith_1979.JPG" class="image" title="Joe Beckwith in 1979"><img alt="Joe Beckwith in 1979" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Joe_Beckwith_1979.JPG/116px-Joe_Beckwith_1979.JPG" decoding="async" width="116" height="170" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Joe_Beckwith_1979.JPG/174px-Joe_Beckwith_1979.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Joe_Beckwith_1979.JPG/232px-Joe_Beckwith_1979.JPG 2x" data-file-width="505" data-file-height="741"></a>

         Joe Beckwith in 1979
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Joe_Beckwith" title="Joe Beckwith">Joe Beckwith</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> was one of only two <a href="/wiki/Relief_pitcher" title="Relief pitcher">relief pitchers</a> used by the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a> to win the <a href="/wiki/1985_World_Series" title="1985 World Series">1985 World Series</a>? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.mlb.com/news/world-series-game-2-storylines/c-155780008">MLB.com</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Joe_Beckwith" title="Joe Beckwith">Joe Beckwith</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> worked in the concrete industry after his Major League Baseball career? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.mlb.com/news/where-are-they-now-1985-royals/c-97965202">MLB.com</a>; <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://dothaneagle.com/sports/college/auburn/auburn-honors-former-mlb-pitcher-joe-beckwith-amidst-cancer-battle/article_d0e129b6-a549-11eb-a0d1-7346b1418735.html"><i>Dothan Eagle</i></a></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

       <dd>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Smoking_in_association_football">Smoking in association football</span></h4> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 121px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Smoking_is_prohibited_at_Goodison_Park_(23699773434).jpg" class="image" title="No smoking sign at Goodison Park"><img alt="No smoking sign at Goodison Park" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Smoking_is_prohibited_at_Goodison_Park_%2823699773434%29.jpg/121px-Smoking_is_prohibited_at_Goodison_Park_%2823699773434%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="121" height="161" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Smoking_is_prohibited_at_Goodison_Park_%2823699773434%29.jpg/182px-Smoking_is_prohibited_at_Goodison_Park_%2823699773434%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Smoking_is_prohibited_at_Goodison_Park_%2823699773434%29.jpg/242px-Smoking_is_prohibited_at_Goodison_Park_%2823699773434%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         No smoking sign at Goodison Park
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FSmoking_in_association_football&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Smoking_in_association_football&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that despite <b><a href="/wiki/Smoking_in_association_football" title="Smoking in association football">smoking in football</a></b> formerly being popular, it has since been banned from the touchline by UEFA? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20200604093834/https://www.uefa.com/insideuefa/news/newsid=134089.html">UEFA</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that an English footballer <b><a href="/wiki/Smoking_in_association_football" title="Smoking in association football">was encouraged to start smoking</a></b> when he became a manager to assert his authority? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.balls.ie/football/whatever-happened-smoking-football-managers-110503">Balls.ie</a></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

       <dd>

        </ul>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lakshmeshwara_Jain_temples">Lakshmeshwara Jain temples</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FLakshmeshwara_Jain_temples&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lakshmeshwara_Jain_temples&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 162px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Lakshmeshwara_Old_Jain_temple_1.jpg" class="image" title="Shanka Basadi"><img alt="Shanka Basadi" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Lakshmeshwara_Old_Jain_temple_1.jpg/162px-Lakshmeshwara_Old_Jain_temple_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="162" height="122" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Lakshmeshwara_Old_Jain_temple_1.jpg/243px-Lakshmeshwara_Old_Jain_temple_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Lakshmeshwara_Old_Jain_temple_1.jpg/324px-Lakshmeshwara_Old_Jain_temple_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304"></a>

       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FIvan_%C5%A0tironja&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 120px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:IvanStironja.jpg" class="image" title="Ivan Štironja in 2009"><img alt="Ivan Štironja in 2009" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/IvanStironja.jpg/120px-IvanStironja.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="163" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/IvanStironja.jpg/180px-IvanStironja.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/IvanStironja.jpg/240px-IvanStironja.jpg 2x" data-file-width="831" data-file-height="1126"></a>

         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that the new bishop of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Kotor" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Kotor">Kotor</a> in <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> <b><a href="/wiki/Ivan_%C5%A0tironja" title="Ivan Štironja">Ivan Štironja</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> originates from <a href="/wiki/Herzegovina" title="Herzegovina">Herzegovina</a>? <small>Source: "Hercegovac i misionar iz Tanzanije biskup u zaljevu hrvatskih svetaca [A Herzegovinian and a missionary from Tanzania is the bishop in the Bay of Croatian Saints]" (<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.vecernji.hr/premium/hercegovac-i-misionar-iz-tanzanije-biskup-u-zaljevu-hrvatskih-svetaca-1482638">[24]</a>)</small></li>

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_May_23"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_May_23">Articles created/expanded on May 23</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on May 23">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mahmut_Bozteke">Mahmut Bozteke</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FMahmut_Bozteke&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mahmut_Bozteke&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Mahmut_Bozteke" title="Mahmut Bozteke">Mahmut Bozteke</a></b>, whose arms were crippled in an accident, started performing <a href="/wiki/Para_Taekwondo" title="Para Taekwondo">Para Taekwondo</a> after his <a href="/wiki/Physical_therapy" title="Physical therapy">physiotherapist</a>'s advise, who discovered that "he can use his legs very well instead"? <small>Source: "<b>Mahmut Bozteke</b>, azmi sayesinde <b>para-tekvando</b>da ...", "... <b>kollar?n?</b> çal???r vaziyetteki traktörün kuyruk miline <b>kapt?rd?</b>. <b>Kopan kollar?</b> ameliyatla dikilen ancak bu uzuvlar?n? diledi?i gibi kullanamad??? için ...", <span class="languageicon">(in Turkish)</span> <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.radikal.com.tr/gaziantep-haber/para-tekvandocu-gencin-hayali-beden-egitimi-ogretmeni-olmak-2893477/">[25]</a>, "... <b>fizyoterapistin</b> "<b>Ayaklar?n? iyi kullan?yorsun, bence iyi tekvando yapars?n</b>" <b>tavsiyesiyle</b> ,..." <span class="languageicon">(in Turkish)</span> <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.aa.com.tr/tr/yasam/yataga-bagimliliktan-paralimpik-oyunlara-uzanan-basari-hikayesi-mahmut-bozteke/2032899">[26]</a> </small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Theater_Trier" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Theater Trier">Theater Trier</a></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <div class="plainlinks hlist">

       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 168px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:ObedDickinsonFamily.jpg" class="image" title="Obed Dickinson with his wife and children."><img alt="Obed Dickinson with his wife and children." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/ObedDickinsonFamily.jpg/168px-ObedDickinsonFamily.jpg" decoding="async" width="168" height="116" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/ObedDickinsonFamily.jpg/252px-ObedDickinsonFamily.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/ObedDickinsonFamily.jpg/336px-ObedDickinsonFamily.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="691"></a>

      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Did_you_know#Cited_hook" title="Wikipedia:Did you know">Cited</a>: <img alt="Red X" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Red_x.svg/13px-Red_x.svg.png" decoding="async" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Red_x.svg/20px-Red_x.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Red_x.svg/26px-Red_x.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"><span style="display: none;">N</span> - "Supported in the article" isn't quite enough here.        <li>Interesting: <img alt="Green tick" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/13px-Green_check.svg.png" decoding="async" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/20px-Green_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/26px-Green_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"><span style="display:none">Y</span></li>

      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FEdward_Rath_III&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Edward_Rath_III" title="Edward Rath III">Edward Rath III</a></b> is a third-generation politician in the <a href="/wiki/Western_New_York" title="Western New York">Western New York</a> region? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://news.wbfo.org/post/third-generation-rath-family-elected-government-post">[27]</a>)</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Edward_Rath_III" title="Edward Rath III">Edward Rath III</a></b> is the son of a politician and the grandson of a politician? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.clarencebee.com/articles/after-more-than-a-decade-in-erie-county-rath-heads-to-albany-to-take-up-his-mothers-former-senate-seat/">[28]</a>)</small></li>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Marie_Antoinette_with_a_Rose">Marie Antoinette with a Rose</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FMarie_Antoinette_with_a_Rose&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Marie_Antoinette_with_a_Rose&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 127px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Louise_Elisabeth_Vig%C3%A9e-Lebrun_-_Marie-Antoinette_dit_%C2%AB_%C3%A0_la_Rose_%C2%BB_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image" title="Marie Antoinette with a Rose by Élisabeth Vigée Le Brun"><img alt="Marie Antoinette with a Rose by Élisabeth Vigée Le Brun" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Louise_Elisabeth_Vig%C3%A9e-Lebrun_-_Marie-Antoinette_dit_%C2%AB_%C3%A0_la_Rose_%C2%BB_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/127px-Louise_Elisabeth_Vig%C3%A9e-Lebrun_-_Marie-Antoinette_dit_%C2%AB_%C3%A0_la_Rose_%C2%BB_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" decoding="async" width="127" height="154" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Louise_Elisabeth_Vig%C3%A9e-Lebrun_-_Marie-Antoinette_dit_%C2%AB_%C3%A0_la_Rose_%C2%BB_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/191px-Louise_Elisabeth_Vig%C3%A9e-Lebrun_-_Marie-Antoinette_dit_%C2%AB_%C3%A0_la_Rose_%C2%BB_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Louise_Elisabeth_Vig%C3%A9e-Lebrun_-_Marie-Antoinette_dit_%C2%AB_%C3%A0_la_Rose_%C2%BB_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/254px-Louise_Elisabeth_Vig%C3%A9e-Lebrun_-_Marie-Antoinette_dit_%C2%AB_%C3%A0_la_Rose_%C2%BB_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3894" data-file-height="4728"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         <i><a href="/wiki/Marie_Antoinette_with_a_Rose" title="Marie Antoinette with a Rose">Marie Antoinette with a Rose</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/%C3%89lisabeth_Vig%C3%A9e_Le_Brun" title="Élisabeth Vigée Le Brun">Élisabeth Vigée Le Brun</a>
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the previous portrait that illustrates <a href="/wiki/Marie_Antoinette" title="Marie Antoinette">Marie Antoinette</a> wearing a <a href="/wiki/Muslin" title="Muslin">muslin</a> dress before <i><b><a href="/wiki/Marie_Antoinette_with_a_Rose" title="Marie Antoinette with a Rose">Marie Antoinette with a Rose</a></b></i> <i>(pictured)</i> was painted, is the subject's favourite dress? <small>Source: "Vigée-Le Brun presented notably a new portrait of the Queen wearing the “gaulle” or “blouse dress”. Adapted to Parisian fashion by the dressmaker Rose Bertin, this muslin dress was the Queen’s favourite one during her stays at the Petit Trianon, away from the court. The visitors of the Salon were shocked by this portrait: in their view the Queen was not dressed as befitted her rank. So the painting was quickly withdrawn. Vigée-Le Brun then quickly painted a second portrait to be exhibited before the end of the Salon." <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://artsandculture.google.com/asset/marie-antoinette-with-the-rose-louise-elisabeth-vig%C3%A9e-lebrun/qwHgKqLoAQb9FQ?hl=en">Google Arts &amp; Culture</a></small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/St._George%27s_Basilica,_Prague" title="Template:Did you know nominations/St. George's Basilica, Prague">St. George's Basilica, Prague</a></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Trisomy_X">Trisomy X</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FTrisomy_X&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Trisomy_X&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that one in a thousand women have <b><a href="/wiki/Trisomy_X" title="Trisomy X">three X chromosomes</a></b>, but only 10% of them know it? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://ojrd.biomedcentral.com/articles/10.1186/1750-1172-5-8">"It is the most common female chromosomal abnormality, occurring in approximately 1 in 1,000 female births. As some individuals are only mildly affected or asymptomatic, it is estimated that only 10% of individuals with trisomy X are actually diagnosed."</a></small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/WHIS" title="Template:Did you know nominations/WHIS">Did you know nominations/WHIS</a></li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: As with <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Pentasomy_X" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Pentasomy X">Did you know nominations/Pentasomy X</a>, this is a messy page history to evaluate, as it was rewritten in userspace and merged into the pre-existing mainspace article. The last pre-expansion diff is <a href="/wiki/Special:PermanentLink/1021839101" title="Special:PermanentLink/1021839101">here</a>, at 4946 B/809 words readable prose size. The expansion at the time of hitting mainspace is <a href="/wiki/Special:PermanentLink/1024671565" title="Special:PermanentLink/1024671565">here</a>, at 29 kB/4513 words readable prose size.</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h4><span id="Jane_Douglass_White.2C_Song_of_the_Women.27s_Army_Corps"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Jane_Douglass_White,_Song_of_the_Women's_Army_Corps">Jane Douglass White, Song of the Women's Army Corps</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FJane_Douglass_White&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( Article history links: <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Jane_Douglass_White&amp;action=history">Jane Douglass White</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Song_of_the_Women%27s_Army_Corps&amp;action=history">Song of the Women's Army Corps</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that before she entered the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">U.S. Army</a> in 1942, <b><a href="/wiki/Jane_Douglass_White" title="Jane Douglass White">Jane Douglass White</a></b> had already composed the tune which would become the official "<b><a href="/wiki/Song_of_the_Women%27s_Army_Corps" title="Song of the Women's Army Corps">Song of the Women's Army Corps</a></b>"? <small><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.newspapers.com/clip/26792095/the-times-herald/">This Associated Press source</a> indicates the subject composed the initial song version the night she was inducted.<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.newspapers.com/clip/78880391/armed-forces-day-presents-official-song/">This newspaper article sums everything else up in one paragraph.</a> This <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.imdb.com/title/tt0046995/soundtrack">normally unreliable source</a> confirms name, status, and authorship in the onscreen movie credits.</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that before she entered the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">U.S. Army</a> in 1942, <b><a href="/wiki/Soldier%27s_show" title="Soldier's show">soldier's show</a></b> songwriter <b><a href="/wiki/Jane_Douglass_White" title="Jane Douglass White">Jane Douglass White</a></b> had already composed the tune which would become the official "<b><a href="/wiki/Song_of_the_Women%27s_Army_Corps" title="Song of the Women's Army Corps">Song of the Women's Army Corps</a></b>"?</li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

       <dd>

         <li><i>Comment</i>: <s>I am sorry for the long sourcing statement. With my newspapers.com account temporarily disabled, I'm unable to find a single source which says this in one fell swoop.       <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Quesabirria">Quesabirria</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FQuesabirria&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Quesabirria&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 159px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Quesabirria_at_Taqueria_La_Hacienda,_Sonoma,_California_-_Sarah_Stierch.jpg" class="image" title="Quesabirria in California"><img alt="Quesabirria in California" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Quesabirria_at_Taqueria_La_Hacienda%2C_Sonoma%2C_California_-_Sarah_Stierch.jpg/159px-Quesabirria_at_Taqueria_La_Hacienda%2C_Sonoma%2C_California_-_Sarah_Stierch.jpg" decoding="async" width="159" height="124" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Quesabirria_at_Taqueria_La_Hacienda%2C_Sonoma%2C_California_-_Sarah_Stierch.jpg/239px-Quesabirria_at_Taqueria_La_Hacienda%2C_Sonoma%2C_California_-_Sarah_Stierch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Quesabirria_at_Taqueria_La_Hacienda%2C_Sonoma%2C_California_-_Sarah_Stierch.jpg/318px-Quesabirria_at_Taqueria_La_Hacienda%2C_Sonoma%2C_California_-_Sarah_Stierch.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3804" data-file-height="2958"></a>

         Quesabirria in California
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Quesabirria" title="Quesabirria">quesabirria</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> became a "full-fledged phenomenon" in the United States through Instagram posts? <sup id="cite_ref-Tsai_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tsai-7">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[4]</a></sup> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that foodies will travel great distances and wait in line for hours to eat <b><a href="/wiki/Quesabirria" title="Quesabirria">quesabirria</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i>? <sup id="cite_ref-Tsai_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tsai-7">[3]</a></sup></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Quesabirria" title="Quesabirria">quesabirria</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> is "a cross between a taco and a quesadilla"? <sup id="cite_ref-Tsai_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tsai-7">[3]</a></sup></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Eye_of_Horus" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Eye of Horus">Template:Did you know nominations/Eye of Horus</a></li>

      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FSimla_Deputation&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

      </div>

       <li>... that one of the arguments made by the <b><a href="/wiki/Simla_Deputation" title="Simla Deputation">Simla Deputation</a></b> for increasing Muslim representation in Indian politics was that they had ruled India under the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal Empire</a>? <small>Panigrahi, Devendra (19 August 2004). India's Partition: The Story of Imperialism in Retreat. Routledge. ISBN 1-135-76812-9. p. 45.</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Simla_Deputation" title="Simla Deputation">Simla Deputation</a></b> was thought by historians to be engineered by the British? <small>Voigt, Johannes H. (April 1965). "Review of Lord Minto and the Indian Nationalist Movement, 1905 to 1910 by Syed Razi Wasti".       <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_May_26"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_May_26">Articles created/expanded on May 26</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on May 26">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span id="Big_Time_Wrestling_.28Boston.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Big_Time_Wrestling_(Boston)">Big Time Wrestling (Boston)</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FBig_Time_Wrestling_%28Boston%29&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Big_Time_Wrestling_%28Boston%29&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Big_Time_Wrestling_(Boston)" title="Big Time Wrestling (Boston)">Big Time Wrestling</a></b> was one the first <a href="/wiki/List_of_outlaw_wrestling_promotions" title="List of outlaw wrestling promotions">"outlaw" wrestling promotions</a> according to <a href="/wiki/Jim_Cornette" title="Jim Cornette">Jim Cornette</a>? <small>Source: <i>Source</i></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that influenced by booker <a href="/wiki/Jack_Pfeffer" class="mw-redirect" title="Jack Pfeffer">Jack Pfeffer</a>, <b><a href="/wiki/Big_Time_Wrestling_(Boston)" title="Big Time Wrestling (Boston)">Big Time Wrestling</a></b> was notorious for using parody "soundalike" wrestlers of the <a href="/wiki/National_Wrestling_Alliance" title="National Wrestling Alliance">National Wrestling Alliance</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Wrestling_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="World Wide Wrestling Federation">World Wide Wrestling Federation</a>? <small>Source: <i>Source</i></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that <a href="/wiki/Bearcat_Wright" title="Bearcat Wright">Bearcat Wright</a> won <b><a href="/wiki/Big_Time_Wrestling_(Boston)" title="Big Time Wrestling (Boston)">Big Time Wrestling</a></b><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s heavyweight championship from <a href="/wiki/Killer_Kowalski" title="Killer Kowalski">Killer Kowalski</a> in 1961, becoming one of the first African-Americans to win a major singles title during the Territory era? <small>Source: <i>Source</i></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT3</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Big_Time_Wrestling_(Boston)" title="Big Time Wrestling (Boston)">Big Time Wrestling</a></b> had a promotional war with the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Wrestling_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="World Wide Wrestling Federation">World Wide Wrestling Federation</a> over the New England wrestling territory during the 1960s? <small>Source: <i>Source</i></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT4</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Big_Time_Wrestling_(Boston)" title="Big Time Wrestling (Boston)">Big Time Wrestling</a></b> opened one of the first <a href="/wiki/Wrestling_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Wrestling school">wrestling schools</a> in the country which produced <a href="/wiki/Les_Thatcher" title="Les Thatcher">Les Thatcher</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rufus_R._Jones" title="Rufus R. Jones">Rufus R. Jones</a> among others? <small>Source: <i>Source</i></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT5</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Big_Time_Wrestling_(Boston)" title="Big Time Wrestling (Boston)">Big Time Wrestling</a></b> was considered a "safe" territory for GLBT wrestlers and <a href="/wiki/Ron_Dupree" title="Ron Dupree">Ron Dupree</a> was able to live openly with his partner? <small>Source: <i>Source</i></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT6</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Big_Time_Wrestling_(Boston)" title="Big Time Wrestling (Boston)">Big Time Wrestling</a></b> featured a wrestling bear called "Black Ozzie" which later escaped shortly after being sold and they joined in a police search and was able to subdue the bear by putting sugar in its mouth? <small>Source: <i>Source</i></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT7</b>:... that one of <b><a href="/wiki/Big_Time_Wrestling_(Boston)" title="Big Time Wrestling (Boston)">Big Time Wrestling</a></b><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s first major attractions was a series of wrestling bouts between Black Ozzie and BTW Women's Champion Alma Mills? <small>Source: <i>Source</i></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT8</b>:... that <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>, then a Massachusetts Senator, and his wife <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Kennedy" class="mw-redirect" title="Jackie Kennedy">Jackie</a> attended <b><a href="/wiki/Big_Time_Wrestling_(Boston)" title="Big Time Wrestling (Boston)">Big Time Wrestling</a></b><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s shows in West Yarmouth, Massachusetts? <small>Source: <i>Source</i></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT9</b>:... that while napping in the locker room, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Pfefer" title="Jack Pfefer">Jack Pfefer</a> was once thrown out of the Boston Arena by a rookie wrestler who mistook him for a homeless man who had wandered in off the street? <small>Source: <i>Source</i></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT10</b>:... that Frankie Scarpa, then a longtime regional star, competed with the up-and-coming <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Sammartino" title="Bruno Sammartino">Bruno Sammartino</a> for the Italian-American fans in Boston during the 1960s? <small>Source: <i>Source</i></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT11</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Big_Time_Wrestling_(Boston)" title="Big Time Wrestling (Boston)">Big Time Wrestling</a></b> closed after its main star Frankie Scarpa died in the ring in 1969? <small>Source: <i>Source</i></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <h4><span id="Battle_of_Sambisa_Forest_.282021.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_of_Sambisa_Forest_(2021)">Battle of Sambisa Forest (2021)</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FBattle_of_Sambisa_Forest_%282021%29&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <a href="/wiki/Boko_Haram" title="Boko Haram">Boko Haram</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Abubakar_Shekau" title="Abubakar Shekau">Abubakar Shekau</a>'s tone indicated that he "was near the end" during a sermon one day before his forces were defeated during the <b><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sambisa_Forest_(2021)" title="Battle of Sambisa Forest (2021)">Battle of Sambisa Forest (2021)</a></b>? <small>Source: "Shekau, for his part, gave a final sermon on the day before his death that has been leaked publicly. He indicated that many of his fighters had been killed and the group was facing calamities. Shekau said he would never be loyal to anybody. His tone also suggested he knew was near the end. However, the dramatic fashion in which he reportedly ended his life evidently took ISWAP by surprise and, for the first time in several years, Nigeria will enter a post-Shekau era." (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://jamestown.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/05/TM-May-24-2021-Issue.pdf?x50264">Killing of Boko Haram Leader Abubakar Shekau Boosts Islamic State in Nigeria, p. 2</a>)</small></li>

      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FStefanina_Moro&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

       <li>... that <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a> honored <b><a href="/wiki/Stefanina_Moro" title="Stefanina Moro">Stefanina Moro</a></b>, a teenage courier in the <a href="/wiki/Italian_resistance_movement" title="Italian resistance movement">Italian resistance</a> who was killed by Nazis, by naming a street after her? <small>Sources: "Dopo l’8 settembre, il boia nazista Friedrich Engel ne fa un luogo di tortura. ... Passano di qui Vannuccio Faralli (che sarà primo sindaco di Genova nel dopoguerra), Luciano Bolis (che racconterà le torture subite in Il mio granello di sabbia) e la staffetta 17enne Stefanina Moro che, dopo le torture, morirà all’ospedale di Asti." <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.corriere.it/cronache/casa-studente-genova-partigiani/index.shtml">Corriere della Sera</a>; "Peraltro in un quartiere, Quezzi, dove le strade e le piazze portano i nomi dei partigiani uccisi (Stefanina Moro, Piero Pinetti e Augusto Merlo, tra altri)." <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.comune.genova.it/content/inizia-dai-bambini-il-70deg-anniversario-del-25-aprile-di-genova">City of Genoa's website</a></small></li>

       <li>... that the art historian <b><a href="/wiki/Birgit_Dahlenburg" title="Birgit Dahlenburg">Birgit Dahlenburg</a></b> was instrumental in the recognition of the Croy Carpet <i>(pictured)</i> from the 16th century as a national heritage? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://wissenschaftliche-sammlungen.de/de/nachrichten/aktuelles/birgit-dahlenburg-1959-2017">[30]</a></small></li>
      </ul>

       <dd>

      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>

        <ul>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Justin_Clarke">Justin Clarke</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FJustin_Clarke&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that following severe injury and the demise of his professional AFL career, <b><a href="/wiki/Justin_Clarke" title="Justin Clarke">Justin Clarke</a></b> turned Rhodes scholar in 2021? <small>Source: University of Queensland <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://www.uq.edu.au/news/article/2020/10/former-lion-turned-student-queensland%E2%80%99s-newest-rhodes-scholar">https://www.uq.edu.au/news/article/2020/10/former-lion-turned-student-queensland%E2%80%99s-newest-rhodes-scholar</a></small>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="111_West_57th_Street">111 West 57th Street</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2F111_West_57th_Street&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=111_West_57th_Street&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 119px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:111_West_57_St.jpg" class="image" title="111 West 57th Street"><img alt="111 West 57th Street" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/111_West_57_St.jpg/119px-111_West_57_St.jpg" decoding="async" width="119" height="164" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/111_West_57_St.jpg/179px-111_West_57_St.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/111_West_57_St.jpg/238px-111_West_57_St.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2264" data-file-height="3128"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         111 West 57th Street
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/111_West_57th_Street" title="111 West 57th Street">111 West 57th Street</a></b>, one of the tallest buildings in the United States, was legally classified as an "alteration" to the existing 16-story Steinway Hall? <small>Source: (1) <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://therealdeal.com/2018/05/16/building-in-the-shadows-3-2m-sf-of-new-construction-being-built-with-this-permit/">Sun, Kevin (May 16, 2018). "Building in the shadows: 3.2M sf of new construction being built with this permit". The Real Deal New York.</a> (2) <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://s-media.nyc.gov/agencies/lpc/lp/2100.pdf">"Steinway Hall" (PDF). New York City Landmarks Preservation Commission. November 13, 2001.</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that the supertall <b><a href="/wiki/111_West_57th_Street" title="111 West 57th Street">111 West 57th Street</a></b> skyscraper in New York City was legally classified as an "alteration" to the existing 16-story Steinway Hall? <small>Source: Same as ALT0</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that a Steinway piano showroom at <b><a href="/wiki/111_West_57th_Street" title="111 West 57th Street">111 West 57th Street</a></b> in New York City was expanded 2,850 percent to become one of the tallest buildings in the United States? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://therealdeal.com/2018/05/16/building-in-the-shadows-3-2m-sf-of-new-construction-being-built-with-this-permit/">Sun, Kevin (May 16, 2018). "Building in the shadows: 3.2M sf of new construction being built with this permit". The Real Deal New York.</a></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT3</b>:... that a Steinway piano showroom at <b><a href="/wiki/111_West_57th_Street" title="111 West 57th Street">111 West 57th Street</a></b> in New York City was expanded 2,850 percent into a supertall tower? <small>Source: Same as ALT2</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT4</b>:... that the <b><a href="/wiki/111_West_57th_Street" title="111 West 57th Street">111 West 57th Street</a></b> tower was nicknamed "Stairway to Heaven" because of the shape of its pinnacle? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.bisnow.com/new-york/news/mixed-use/inside-the-supertalls-111-west-57th-street-67035">Mazzara, Benjamin (October 29, 2016). "Inside The Supertalls: 111 West 57th Street". Bisnow</a></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT5</b>:... that the developers of <b><a href="/wiki/111_West_57th_Street" title="111 West 57th Street">111 West 57th Street</a></b> intended for it to become New York City's tallest building constructed with non-union labor? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.crainsnewyork.com/article/20150114/REAL_ESTATE/301119992/nonunion-west-57th-st-spire-aims-to-shatter-record">Geiger, Daniel (January 13, 2015). "Nonunion West 57th St. spire aims to shatter record". Crain's New York. </a></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FLos_Campitos_Reservoir&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 162px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_2021_006.jpg" class="image" title="The dam and empty reservoir in 2021"><img alt="The dam and empty reservoir in 2021" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_2021_006.jpg/162px-Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_2021_006.jpg" decoding="async" width="162" height="122" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_2021_006.jpg/243px-Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_2021_006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_2021_006.jpg/324px-Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_2021_006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></a>

         The dam and empty reservoir in 2021

       <li>... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Los_Campitos_Reservoir" title="Los Campitos Reservoir">Los Campitos Reservoir</a></b> in Tenerife has never held water? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.eldia.es/santa-cruz-de-tenerife/2021/02/28/agua-santa-cruz-embalses-35959237.html">[33]</a> (Spanish), <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://ropdigital.ciccp.es/detalle_articulo.php?registro=19143&amp;anio=2012&amp;numero_revista=3530">[34]</a> (PDF is in English, see Fig. 6)</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that after constructing a 54-metre-high (177&nbsp;ft) dam, it was discovered that the basin of the <b><a href="/wiki/Los_Campitos_Reservoir" title="Los Campitos Reservoir">Los Campitos Reservoir</a></b> was not waterproof? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.eldia.es/santa-cruz-de-tenerife/2021/02/28/agua-santa-cruz-embalses-35959237.html">[35]</a> (Spanish), <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://ropdigital.ciccp.es/detalle_articulo.php?registro=19143&amp;anio=2012&amp;numero_revista=3530">[36]</a> (PDF is in English, see Fig. 6)</small></li>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_ocean_convection">Open ocean convection</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FOpen_ocean_convection&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Open_ocean_convection&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that in the North Atlantic, <b><a href="/wiki/Open_ocean_convection" title="Open ocean convection">open ocean convection</a></b>, the mixing of deep and surface waters that plays a crucial role in global climate, has decreased in response to global warming? <small>Sources: "Open-ocean deep convection...occurs at only three known northern hemisphere sites...as well as in the Weddell Sea...These sites, of small geographical extent, are of great importance for ocean climate." (Wadhams et al 2002), and "In EC-Earth [an earth system model], just as observations suggest, LSDC [Labrador Sea deep convection] is subject to unpredictable and strong variability, with the resumption of deep convection after shutdowns of sometimes several years. Note that the likelihood of shutdowns of about one decade in the model increases with global warming (Fig. 6), but seems to be underestimated with regards to observations. For example, Yashayaev and Loder (2009) showed that 2008 was the first year with deep convection in the Labrador Sea since 1994" (Brodeau and Koenigk 2016).</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Open_ocean_convection" title="Open ocean convection">open ocean convection</a></b>, the mixing of deep and surface waters, plays a crucial role in global climate? <small>Sources: "Open-ocean deep convection...occurs at only three known northern hemisphere sites...as well as in the Weddell Sea...These sites, of small geographical extent, are of great importance for ocean climate" (Wadhams et al 2002).</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/1928_Austin_city_plan#footer" title="Template:Did you know nominations/1928 Austin city plan">1928 Austin city plan</a></li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: <a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Dandelion11&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Dandelion11 (page does not exist)">Dandelion11</a> created the draft on 15 May 2021, which <a href="/wiki/User:Chidgk1" title="User:Chidgk1">Chidgk1</a> moved to the mainspace on 30 May 2021.</li>
        </ul>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Nilima_Arun_Kshirsagar">Nilima Arun Kshirsagar</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FNilima_Arun_Kshirsagar&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nilima_Arun_Kshirsagar&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the drug Lipoosomal Amphotericin-b, used to treat Indian <a href="/wiki/Black_fungus_(COVID-19_condition)" class="mw-redirect" title="Black fungus (COVID-19 condition)">Mucormycosis epidemic of 2021</a> was indigenously developed and patented by <b><a href="/wiki/Nilima_Arun_Kshirsagar" title="Nilima Arun Kshirsagar">Nilima Arun Kshirsagar</a></b> in 1993? <small>Source: For indigenously developed and patented <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jpgmonline.com/article.asp?issn=0022-3859;year=2005;volume=51;issue=5;spage=5;epage=15;aulast=Kshirsagar">Liposomal drug delivery system from laboratory to clinic</a> Source: used to treat Indian Mucormycosis epidemic of 2021 <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.newindianexpress.com/states/kerala/2021/may/30/kerala-running-short-of-medication-to-meet-black-fungus-threat-2309322.html">kerala running short of medication to meet black fungus threat</a></small></li>
      </ul> 
      <p><small>Created by <a href="/wiki/User:Sachinvenga" title="User:Sachinvenga">Sachinvenga</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Sachinvenga" title="User talk:Sachinvenga">talk</a>). Self-nominated at 12:29, 30 May 2021 (UTC).</small> </p>

      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 109px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Edwards_Davis_-_1919_MPW.jpg" class="image" title="Edwards Davis"><img alt="Edwards Davis" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Edwards_Davis_-_1919_MPW.jpg/109px-Edwards_Davis_-_1919_MPW.jpg" decoding="async" width="109" height="179" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Edwards_Davis_-_1919_MPW.jpg/164px-Edwards_Davis_-_1919_MPW.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Edwards_Davis_-_1919_MPW.jpg/218px-Edwards_Davis_-_1919_MPW.jpg 2x" data-file-width="252" data-file-height="413"></a>

       <li>... that before a career in stage and film, <b><a href="/wiki/Edwards_Davis" title="Edwards Davis">Edwards Davis</a></b> (<i>pictured</i>) was an ordained minister known for dancing in his pulpit? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://cdnc.ucr.edu/?a=d&amp;d=DCS19001229.2.28">"Edwards Davis, M. A., who earned fame in an Oakland church by dancing about his pulpit wearing fashionable evening dress and doing other amusing stunts for the edification of his parishoners, is now engaged in legitimate drama"</a></small></li>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Carolyn_Huntoon">Carolyn Huntoon</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FCarolyn_Huntoon&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Carolyn_Huntoon&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 120px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Dr._Carolyn_Huntoon,_JSC_Director.jpg" class="image" title="Carolyn Huntoon"><img alt="Carolyn Huntoon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Dr._Carolyn_Huntoon%2C_JSC_Director.jpg/120px-Dr._Carolyn_Huntoon%2C_JSC_Director.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="164" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Dr._Carolyn_Huntoon%2C_JSC_Director.jpg/180px-Dr._Carolyn_Huntoon%2C_JSC_Director.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Dr._Carolyn_Huntoon%2C_JSC_Director.jpg/240px-Dr._Carolyn_Huntoon%2C_JSC_Director.jpg 2x" data-file-width="416" data-file-height="568"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Carolyn Huntoon
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Carolyn_Huntoon" title="Carolyn Huntoon">Carolyn Huntoon</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> was the first woman to serve as the director of the <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Space_Center" title="Johnson Space Center">Johnson Space Center</a>? <small>Source: "NASA has named Carolyn Huntoon director of the Johnson Space Center in Houston. Huntoon, who began her career with the National Aeronautics and Space Administration in 1970 and served most recently as director of Space and Life Sciences at the center, is the first female director of the command center of the U.S. space program." <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.chicagotribune.com/news/ct-xpm-1994-01-23-9401230455-story.html">[37]</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... <b><a href="/wiki/Carolyn_Huntoon" title="Carolyn Huntoon">Carolyn Huntoon</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> joined NASA as a result of her master's thesis on <a href="/wiki/Aldosterone" title="Aldosterone">aldosterone</a>, a salt-retaining hormone produced by the adrenal gland? <small>Source: " as part of my master’s thesis, we decided to study the salt-retaining hormone, [aldosterone,] because fluid and electrolyte balance had been a big issue with space flight. The crews were coming back in a fainting mode after they reentered. Their metabolism was not normal right after reentry, and we were trying to find out why. I set up an analysis for aldosterone, which is a salt-retaining hormone of the adrenal gland, there at Baylor College of Medicine, and that was for my master’s thesis. I did the analysis on normal subjects and on astronauts and for the first time documented that people that go into space come back with a very high aldosterone level, trying obviously to conserve sodium which had been lost during space flight. So that sort of was the enticement for me to get involved with NASA." <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://historycollection.jsc.nasa.gov/JSCHistoryPortal/history/oral_histories/HuntoonCL/HuntoonCL_6-5-02.htm">[38]</a></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Ren%C3%A9e_Erd%C5%91s" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Renée Erd?s">Template:Did you know nominations/Renée Erd?s</a></li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: Article was deleted for copyvio and has been re-created with all-new text.</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Thelma_Akana_Harrison">Thelma Akana Harrison</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FThelma_Akana_Harrison&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that the <i><a href="/wiki/Honolulu_Star-Bulletin" title="Honolulu Star-Bulletin">Honolulu Star-Bulletin</a></i> described <b><a href="/wiki/Thelma_Akana_Harrison" title="Thelma Akana Harrison">Thelma Akana Harrison</a></b> as "volatile" in 1950, and as "brilliant" and "vivacious" in 1951? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.newspapers.com/clip/78724825/honolulu-star-bulletin/">1950</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.newspapers.com/clip/78724560/honolulu-star-bulletin/">1951</a></small></li>

      <h4><span id="Arthur_Blake_.28actor.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Arthur_Blake_(actor)">Arthur Blake (actor)</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FArthur_Blake_%28actor%29&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Arthur_Blake_%28actor%29&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that actor <b><a href="/wiki/Arthur_Blake_(actor)" title="Arthur Blake (actor)">Arthur Blake</a></b> was famous for his female impersonations of <a href="/wiki/Bette_Davis" title="Bette Davis">Bette Davis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carmen_Miranda" title="Carmen Miranda">Carmen Miranda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Roosevelt" title="Eleanor Roosevelt">Eleanor Roosevelt</a>? <small>Source: 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFJacob_Smith2011" class="citation book cs1">Jacob Smith (2011). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.google.com/books/edition/Spoken_Word/cSU1e-XStVcC?hl=en&amp;gbpv=1&amp;bsq=%22Arthur%20Blake%22"><i>Spoken Word: Postwar American Phonograph Culture</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/University_of_California_Press" title="University of California Press">University of California Press</a>. p.&nbsp;126-129.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Spoken+Word%3A+Postwar+American+Phonograph+Culture&amp;rft.pages=126-129&amp;rft.pub=University+of+California+Press&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft.au=Jacob+Smith&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.google.com%2Fbooks%2Fedition%2FSpoken_Word%2FcSU1e-XStVcC%3Fhl%3Den%26gbpv%3D1%26bsq%3D%2522Arthur%2520Blake%2522&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know" class="Z3988"></span> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFKathryn_Bishop-Sanchez2021" class="citation book cs1">Kathryn Bishop-Sanchez (2021). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.google.com/books/edition/Creating_Carmen_Miranda/TbwpEAAAQBAJ?hl=en&amp;gbpv=1&amp;dq=%22arthur+blake%22+%22diplomatic+courier%22&amp;pg=PT329&amp;printsec=frontcover"><i>Creating Carmen Miranda: Race, Camp, and Transnational Stardom</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/Vanderbilt_University_Press" title="Vanderbilt University Press">Vanderbilt University Press</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Creating+Carmen+Miranda%3A+Race%2C+Camp%2C+and+Transnational+Stardom&amp;rft.pub=Vanderbilt+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2021&amp;rft.au=Kathryn+Bishop-Sanchez&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.google.com%2Fbooks%2Fedition%2FCreating_Carmen_Miranda%2FTbwpEAAAQBAJ%3Fhl%3Den%26gbpv%3D1%26dq%3D%2522arthur%2Bblake%2522%2B%2522diplomatic%2Bcourier%2522%26pg%3DPT329%26printsec%3Dfrontcover&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know" class="Z3988"></span>)</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Arthur_Blake_(actor)" title="Arthur Blake (actor)">Arthur Blake</a></b>, famous for impersonating <a href="/wiki/Bette_Davis" title="Bette Davis">Bette Davis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carmen_Miranda" title="Carmen Miranda">Carmen Miranda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Roosevelt" title="Eleanor Roosevelt">Eleanor Roosevelt</a>, was put out of work by the <a href="/wiki/Cocoanut_Grove_fire" title="Cocoanut Grove fire">Cocoanut Grove fire</a> in 1942? <small>Source: See the two sources above and 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation book cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=ngwEAAAAMBAJ&amp;pg=PT10&amp;dq=%22Arthur+Blake%22+%22+Cocoanut+Grove%22&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ved=2ahUKEwjv17iAjPXwAhXKXc0KHd21AqMQ6AEwAHoECAIQAg#v=onepage&amp;q=%22Arthur%20Blake%22%20%22%20Cocoanut%20Grove%22&amp;f=false"><i>Nightclubs—Vaudeville: Thrown Out of Work</i></a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i>.       <h4><span id="Wanamaker_expeditions.2C_Joseph_K._Dixon"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Wanamaker_expeditions,_Joseph_K._Dixon">Wanamaker expeditions, Joseph K. Dixon</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FWanamaker_expeditions&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( Article history links: <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wanamaker_expeditions&amp;action=history">Wanamaker expeditions</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Joseph_K._Dixon&amp;action=history">Joseph K. Dixon</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the third <b><a href="/wiki/Wanamaker_expeditions" title="Wanamaker expeditions">Wanamaker expedition</a></b>, led by <b><a href="/wiki/Joseph_K._Dixon" title="Joseph K. Dixon">Joseph K.       <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ivan_Gates">Ivan Gates</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FIvan_Gates&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Police_Department" title="San Francisco Police Department">San Francisco Police</a> officer (and future <a href="/wiki/Barnstorming" title="Barnstorming">barnstormer</a>) <b><a href="/wiki/Ivan_R._Gates" title="Ivan R. Gates">Ivan R. Gates</a></b> was the first to transport a prisoner by air, on November 1, 1919? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.newspapers.com/clip/78615997/first-prisoner-by-air/"><i>Boston Globe</i></a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.newspapers.com/clip/78646992/photo-of-first-prisoner-transport-by-air/"><i>Atlanta Constitution</i></a></small></li>

      <p><small>Created by <a href="/wiki/User:Clarityfiend" title="User:Clarityfiend">Clarityfiend</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Clarityfiend" title="User talk:Clarityfiend">talk</a>). Self-nominated at 20:12, 30 May 2021 (UTC).</small> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><s><b>Comment</b>. I was only 99.9% sure the "Ivan Gates" referred to in most newspaper articles was this person. It was (very) remotely possible that there were two of the same uncommon name who just happened to be pilots in San Francisco, but then I found <s>an obscure newspaper</s> two newspapers, the <i>Atlanta Constitution</i> and the obscure <i>Napa Daily Journal</i>, that did specify that it was "Ivan R. Gates".</s> <a href="/wiki/User:Clarityfiend" title="User:Clarityfiend">Clarityfiend</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Clarityfiend" title="User talk:Clarityfiend">talk</a>) 02:12, 31 May 2021 (UTC)</li> 
         <li><s><b>Addendum</b>. The <i>San Francisco Examiner</i> article has a (somewhat blurry) photo of the pilot. The profile (especially the chin) looks similar to the one in a <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.google.com/search?q=%22Ivan+R.+Gates%22&amp;rlz=1C1CHBD_enCA810CA810&amp;sxsrf=ALeKk02_YQZ0i4la2A34EAlHCLHVDe570A:1622427282501&amp;source=lnms&amp;tbm=isch&amp;sa=X&amp;ved=2ahUKEwjKmOPO7PLwAhUEu54KHfapDD8Q_AUoAnoECAEQBA&amp;biw=1346&amp;bih=712#imgrc=V1b_F0YU0-g8vM">later photo in the Wright State University collection</a>. </s> <a href="/wiki/User:Clarityfiend" title="User:Clarityfiend">Clarityfiend</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Clarityfiend" title="User talk:Clarityfiend">talk</a>) 02:26, 31 May 2021 (UTC)</li> 
         <li><b>Eureka!</b> The <i>New York Daily News</i> obituary confirms that the barnstormer was the pioneering police pilot. The much clearer photo of him handling off the miscreant to his chief of police cinches it. <a href="/wiki/User:Clarityfiend" title="User:Clarityfiend">Clarityfiend</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Clarityfiend" title="User talk:Clarityfiend">talk</a>) 10:36, 4 June 2021 (UTC)</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
