      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Socratic_philosophy">Pre-Socratic philosophy</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FPre-Socratic_philosophy&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Pre-Socratic_philosophy&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that a common feature of the <b><a href="/wiki/Pre-Socratic_philosophy" title="Pre-Socratic philosophy">pre-Socratic philosophy</a></b> was the attempt to explain the <a href="/wiki/Kosmos" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosmos">Kosmos</a> without invoking theism? <small> Barnes p16-17&nbsp;: "Still less was it a series of events determined by the will- or the caprice - of the gods. The Presocratics were not, so far as we can tell, atheists: they allowed the gods into their brave new world, and some of them attempted to produce an improved, rationalized, theology in place of the anthropomorphic divinities of the Olympian pantheon. But they removed some of the traditional functions from the gods. Thunder was explained sCientifically, in naturalistic terms - it was no longer a noise .6 INTRODUCTION made by a minatory Zeus. Iris was the goddess.ofthe rainbow, but Xenophanes insisted that Iris or the rainbow was in reality nothing but a multicoloured cloud. Most importantly, the Presocratic gods -like the gods of Aristotle and even of that arch theist Plato - do not interfere with the natural world. The world is orderly without being divinely run. Its order is intrinsic: the internal principles of nature are sufficient to explain its structure and its history. For the happenings that constitute the world's history are not mere brute events, to be recorded and admired. They are structured events which fit together and interconnect. And the patterns of their interconnections provide the truly explanatory account of the world.</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that preeminent philosopher <a href="/wiki/Karl_Popper" title="Karl Popper">Karl Popper</a> traced the roots of western civilization to <b><a href="/wiki/Pre-Socratic_philosophy" title="Pre-Socratic philosophy">pre-Socratic philosophy</a></b>? <small>In an important article Back to Presocratics (1958), Karl Popper writes: "There can be little doubt that the Greek tradition of philosophical criticism had its main source in Ionia ... It thus leads the tradition which created the rational or scientific attitude, and with it our Western civilization, the only civilization, which is based upon science (though, of course, not upon science alone". Source: Original text can be found in Vamvacas 2013, as in article.</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p><small>Improved to Good Article status by <a href="/wiki/User:Cinadon36" title="User:Cinadon36">Cinadon36</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Cinadon36" title="User talk:Cinadon36">talk</a>). Self-nominated at 09:29, 1 June 2021 (UTC).</small> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_question.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol question.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/16px-Symbol_question.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/24px-Symbol_question.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/32px-Symbol_question.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> A long, recently promoted good article and I don't disagree with that decision. I have two small suggestions on the article content: the statement "
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r989825325"><q class="inline-quote-talk">The pre-Socratic intellectual revolution liberated the human mind from the mythical world and initiated a march towards reason and scientific thought that yielded modern western philosophy and science.</q>" might come off as tendentious to a general reader—DYK articles must be neutral—and would probably benefit from having an authority for that claim stated in the text itself, and (very minor) footnote 140 with the David Sedley comment needs tidying. Similarities detected on Earwig are just shared citations from the looks of it. I do just have a couple of problems with the hooks:<br>On <b>ALT0</b>, (1) Some straightforward stylistic points: "the" needs to be deleted from "the pre-Socratic philosophy", and "cosmos" should be spelled normally since it just redirects to <a href="/wiki/Cosmos" title="Cosmos">cosmos</a> anyway and isn't explained as being something substantively different from the English term.<br>(2) More generally, though, I think the word "theism" might be misleading: <i>theism</i> has modern baggage and refers to a kind of belief system, but Barnes's point is more straightforwardly that they (and "even ... that archtheist Plato") don't refer to the intervention of the gods in their accounts of nature.<br>(3) Optional suggestion. For general reader interest I think it would be worth including Barnes's argument on the previous page that this is the <i>earliest</i> instance of this kind of thinking. This is already noted in the article ("
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r989825325"><q class="inline-quote-talk">The pre-Socratics were the first to attempt to provide reductive explanations for a plethora of natural phenomena.</q>") Taking account of all that, I would propose a hook like: "... that <b><a href="/wiki/Pre-Socratic_philosophy" title="Pre-Socratic philosophy">pre-Socratic philosophy</a></b> included some of the earliest attempts to explain the <a href="/wiki/Cosmos" title="Cosmos">cosmos</a> as an ordered system without reference to the gods?".<br><b>ALT1</b> looks OK, but instead of the perhaps POV phrase "preeminent philosopher" I would simply say "the philosopher", and "Western" in "Western civilization" should be capitalized and the phrase linked to the article at <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western culture</a>. I'd prefer ALT0 if adjusted per at least (1) and (2). Phew! —<a href="/wiki/User:Nizolan" title="User:Nizolan">Nizolan</a> <sup>(<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Nizolan" title="User talk:Nizolan">talk</a> · <a href="/wiki/Special:Contributions/Nizolan" title="Special:Contributions/Nizolan">c.</a>)</sup> 20:15, 5 June 2021 (UTC)</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h4><span id="Biderman.27s_Chart_of_Coercion"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Biderman's_Chart_of_Coercion">Biderman's Chart of Coercion</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FBiderman%27s_Chart_of_Coercion&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 140px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Camp_x-ray_detainees.jpg" class="image" title="Prisoners at Guantanamo Bay"><img alt="Prisoners at Guantanamo Bay" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Camp_x-ray_detainees.jpg/140px-Camp_x-ray_detainees.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="140" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Camp_x-ray_detainees.jpg/210px-Camp_x-ray_detainees.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Camp_x-ray_detainees.jpg/280px-Camp_x-ray_detainees.jpg 2x" data-file-width="684" data-file-height="685"></a>

         Prisoners at Guantanamo Bay
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that, although created to understand Chinese psychological torture of <a href="/wiki/Korean_War_POWs_detained_in_North_Korea" title="Korean War POWs detained in North Korea">American POWs</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>, <b><a href="/wiki/Biderman%27s_Chart_of_Coercion" title="Biderman's Chart of Coercion">Biderman's Chart of Coercion</a></b> was utilized by American interrogators to administer <a href="/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay_detention_camp" title="Guantanamo Bay detention camp">Guantanamo Bay detention camp</a>? <small>Source: multiple</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that ...? <small>Source: "You are strongly encouraged to quote the source text supporting each hook" (and [link] the source, or cite it briefly without using citation templates)</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_Kaai_Hayes">Flora Kaai Hayes</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FFlora_Kaai_Hayes&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Flora_Kaai_Hayes&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that in a 1922 <a href="/wiki/Letter_to_the_editor" title="Letter to the editor">letter to the editor</a>, <b><a href="/wiki/Flora_Kaai_Hayes" title="Flora Kaai Hayes">Flora Kaai Hayes</a></b> defended the morality of <a href="/wiki/Hula" title="Hula">hula</a> compared to the "bosom to bosom, thigh to thigh dances" seen on <a href="/wiki/Steamboat" title="Steamboat">steamboats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roof_garden" title="Roof garden">roof gardens</a> at the time? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.newspapers.com/clip/78813587/the-honolulu-advertiser/">The Honolulu Advertiser</a>, rightmost column, about halfway down</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that Hawaiian legislator <b><a href="/wiki/Flora_Kaai_Hayes" title="Flora Kaai Hayes">Flora Kaai Hayes</a></b> was given the <a href="/wiki/Temple_Emanu-El_(Honolulu)#The_Kalakaua_Torah_and_yad" title="Temple Emanu-El (Honolulu)">Kal?kaua Torah</a> after the death of <a href="/wiki/Abigail_Campbell_Kaw%C4%81nanakoa" title="Abigail Campbell Kaw?nanakoa">Princess Abigail Kaw?nanakoa</a>, and owned it until her own death? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.newspapers.com/clip/78813146/the-honolulu-advertiser/">The Honolulu Advertiser</a>, center column</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Flora_Kaai_Hayes" title="Flora Kaai Hayes">Flora Kaai Hayes</a></b>, who would later serve in the <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_State_Legislature" title="Hawaii State Legislature">Hawaii Territorial House</a>, stopped in <a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">Hollywood</a> to act in 1937 film <a href="/wiki/The_Hurricane_(1937_film)" title="The Hurricane (1937 film)"><i>The Hurricane</i></a> on her way back to Hawaii from a conference in Virginia? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.newspapers.com/clip/9308874/the-honolulu-advertiser/">The Honolulu Advertiser</a>, photo caption</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

       <dd>

      <h4><span id="10_West_56th_Street.2C_12_West_56th_Street"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="10_West_56th_Street,_12_West_56th_Street">10 West 56th Street, 12 West 56th Street</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2F10_West_56th_Street&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( Article history links: <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=10_West_56th_Street&amp;action=history">10 West 56th Street</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=12_West_56th_Street&amp;action=history">12 West 56th Street</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 162px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:W_56_St_Apr_2021_36.jpg" class="image" title="10 (left) and 12 West 56th Street (right)"><img alt="10 (left) and 12 West 56th Street (right)" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/W_56_St_Apr_2021_36.jpg/162px-W_56_St_Apr_2021_36.jpg" decoding="async" width="162" height="122" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/W_56_St_Apr_2021_36.jpg/243px-W_56_St_Apr_2021_36.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/W_56_St_Apr_2021_36.jpg/324px-W_56_St_Apr_2021_36.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         10 (left) and 12 West 56th Street (right)
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that though the townhouses at <b><a href="/wiki/10_West_56th_Street" title="10 West 56th Street">10</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/12_West_56th_Street" title="12 West 56th Street">12 West 56th Street</a></b> had been planned jointly for two business partners, number 10 was built in a different style because it was delayed by two years? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2007/04/08/realestate/08scap.html">Gray, Christopher (April 8, 2007). "One Dances the Cancan, the Other the Minuet". The New York Times.</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that the townhouses at <b><a href="/wiki/10_West_56th_Street" title="10 West 56th Street">10</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/12_West_56th_Street" title="12 West 56th Street">12 West 56th Street</a></b>, planned jointly for two business partners, were designed in different styles because of a covenant delaying construction on number 10? <small>Source: Gray 2007</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that stockbroker <a href="/wiki/H._B._Hollins" title="H. B. Hollins">H. B. Hollins</a> planned his house at <b><a href="/wiki/12_West_56th_Street" title="12 West 56th Street">12 West 56th Street</a></b>, now an Argentine consulate, in a different style than his business partner Frederick Edey at <b><a href="/wiki/10_West_56th_Street" title="10 West 56th Street">number 10</a></b>? <small>Source: Gray 2007</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT3</b>:... that the townhouses at <b><a href="/wiki/10_West_56th_Street" title="10 West 56th Street">10</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/12_West_56th_Street" title="12 West 56th Street">12 West 56th Street</a></b>, planned jointly for two business partners, were described as being "paired in an uneasy dance" due to their differing architectural styles? <small>Source: Gray 2007</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT4</b>:... that <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Slim" title="Carlos Slim">Carlos Slim</a>'s New York City townhouse at <b><a href="/wiki/10_West_56th_Street" title="10 West 56th Street">10 West 56th Street</a></b> and the Argentine consulate <b><a href="/wiki/12_West_56th_Street" title="12 West 56th Street">next door</a></b> were developed jointly for two Wall Street business partners? <small>Source: Gray 2007; <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://observer.com/2011/05/carlos-slim-sets-up-shop-on-56th-street/">"Carlos Slim Sets Up Shop on 56th Street". Observer. May 24, 2011.</a></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Anis_Al-Hujjaj">Anis Al-Hujjaj</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FAnis_Al-Hujjaj&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Anis_Al-Hujjaj&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 154px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Khalili_Collection_Hajj_and_Arts_of_Pilgrimage_MSS_1025_f3b_CROP.jpg" class="image" title="Illustration from the Anis Al-Hujjaj"><img alt="Illustration from the Anis Al-Hujjaj" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Khalili_Collection_Hajj_and_Arts_of_Pilgrimage_MSS_1025_f3b_CROP.jpg/154px-Khalili_Collection_Hajj_and_Arts_of_Pilgrimage_MSS_1025_f3b_CROP.jpg" decoding="async" width="154" height="127" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Khalili_Collection_Hajj_and_Arts_of_Pilgrimage_MSS_1025_f3b_CROP.jpg/231px-Khalili_Collection_Hajj_and_Arts_of_Pilgrimage_MSS_1025_f3b_CROP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Khalili_Collection_Hajj_and_Arts_of_Pilgrimage_MSS_1025_f3b_CROP.jpg/308px-Khalili_Collection_Hajj_and_Arts_of_Pilgrimage_MSS_1025_f3b_CROP.jpg 2x" data-file-width="464" data-file-height="383"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Illustration from the <i>Anis Al-Hujjaj</i>
        </div>

      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that a 17th-century illustrated manuscript of the <i><b><a href="/wiki/Anis_Al-Hujjaj" title="Anis Al-Hujjaj">Anis Al-Hujjaj</a></b></i> shows pilgrims sailing from the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a> to <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabia</a> <i>(pictured)</i>? <small>Source: "The 17th-century guide of Anis al-hujjaj (The Pilgrim’s Companion) by Safi ibn Vali has some impressive images of pilgrim ships (c. 1677–80); one of which depicts vessels setting off from the city of Surat. [...] it is not clear which month or year Safi ibn Vali set off on board Salamat Ras from Surat to Jedda;" Agius (2013)</small></li>
      </ul>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Forest_in_Turkey">Forest in Turkey</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FForest_in_Turkey&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Forest_in_Turkey&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <a href="/wiki/Panthera_pardus_tulliana" title="Panthera pardus tulliana">leopards</a> live in the <b><a href="/wiki/Forest_in_Turkey" title="Forest in Turkey">forest in Turkey</a></b>? <small>Source:
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFKarata?,_A.Bulut,_?.Akbaba,_B.2021" class="citation journal cs1">Karata?, A.; Bulut, ?. &amp; Akbaba, B. (2021). "Camera trap records confirm the survival of the Leopard (<i>Panthera pardus</i> L., 1758) in eastern Turkey (Mammalia: Felidae)". <i>Zoology in the Middle East</i>. <a href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1080%2F09397140.2021.1924419">10.1080/09397140.2021.1924419</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Zoology+in+the+Middle+East&amp;rft.atitle=Camera+trap+records+confirm+the+survival+of+the+Leopard+%28Panthera+pardus+L.%2C+1758%29+in+eastern+Turkey+%28Mammalia%3A+Felidae%29&amp;rft.date=2021&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1080%2F09397140.2021.1924419&amp;rft.au=Karata%C5%9F%2C+A.&amp;rft.au=Bulut%2C+%C5%9E.&amp;rft.au=Akbaba%2C+B.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know" class="Z3988"></span></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that <a href="/wiki/Panthera_pardus_tulliana" title="Panthera pardus tulliana">leopards</a> roam the <b><a href="/wiki/Forest_in_Turkey" title="Forest in Turkey">forest in Turkey</a></b>? <small>Source:
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFKarata?,_A.Bulut,_?.Akbaba,_B.2021" class="citation journal cs1">Karata?, A.; Bulut, ?. &amp; Akbaba, B. (2021). The article cites sources (although there is <a href="/wiki/Help:CS1_errors#bad_date" title="Help:CS1 errors">CS1 error</a> in reference [9]). A <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Did_you_know#QPQ" title="Wikipedia:Did you know">QPQ</a> is done. The hook is under 200 characters (43 characters), is cited (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.tandfonline.com/doi/abs/10.1080/09397140.2021.1924419?journalCode=tzme20">1</a>), and meets the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Did_you_know#hookformat" title="Wikipedia:Did you know">formatting guidelines</a>. But I guess the hook isn't interesting <i>to a broad audience</i>. The source shows that "
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r989825325"><q class="inline-quote-talk">the leopards were extinct or on the verge of extinction in Turkey towards the end of the 20th century, but recent photographic evidence proves their survival.</q>" The fact that leopards live in the forest in Turkey needs to be rephrased to make the hook interesting. <a href="/wiki/User:Kavyansh.Singh" title="User:Kavyansh.Singh">Kavyansh.Singh</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Kavyansh.Singh" title="User talk:Kavyansh.Singh">talk</a>) 04:41, 5 June 2021 (UTC)</li>

                Hi <a href="/wiki/User:Chidgk1" title="User:Chidgk1">Chidgk1</a>, thanks for your contribution, but I am still concerned about hook, which is not interesting <i>to a broad audience</i>. Leopards living or roaming in forest of Turkey doesn't grab attention, until they have been recently found, and were previously considered extinct. I suggest the following hook:
                <br>"... that recent photographic record confirms existence of <a href="/wiki/Panthera_pardus_tulliana" title="Panthera pardus tulliana">leopards</a> in <b><a href="/wiki/Forest_in_Turkey" title="Forest in Turkey">Turkey's forest</a></b>, which were considered to be <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinct</a> in late 20th century?"
                <br> If you consider selecting this hook, the same changed need to be made in article too. Thanks! <a href="/wiki/User:Kavyansh.Singh" title="User:Kavyansh.Singh">Kavyansh.Singh</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Kavyansh.Singh" title="User talk:Kavyansh.Singh">talk</a>) 07:06, 5 June 2021 (UTC)

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ita_Ekpenyon">Ita Ekpenyon</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FIta_Ekpenyon&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ita_Ekpenyon&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Ita_Ekpenyon" title="Ita Ekpenyon">Ita Ekpenyon</a></b> is the only known black <a href="/wiki/Air_raid_warden" class="mw-redirect" title="Air raid warden">air raid warden</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Blitz" title="The Blitz">the Blitz</a>? <small>"Westminster Council’s lead education officer Peter Daniel saw it and realised it showed Ita Ekpenyon – the only recorded black air raid warden at a Remembrance Day march 1941." from: 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFGraham2010" class="citation news cs1">Graham, Georgia (8 October 2010). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.hamhigh.co.uk/things-to-do/black-war-hero-hailed-by-young-animators-3412948">"Black war hero hailed by young animators"</a>. <i>Hampstead Highgate Express</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">28 May</span> 2021</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Hampstead+Highgate+Express&amp;rft.atitle=Black+war+hero+hailed+by+young+animators&amp;rft.date=2010-10-08&amp;rft.aulast=Graham&amp;rft.aufirst=Georgia&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hamhigh.co.uk%2Fthings-to-do%2Fblack-war-hero-hailed-by-young-animators-3412948&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know" class="Z3988"></span></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Ita_Ekpenyon" title="Ita Ekpenyon">Ita Ekpenyon</a></b> coached American actor <a href="/wiki/Paul_Robeson" title="Paul Robeson">Paul Robeson</a> in speaking the <a href="/wiki/Efik_language" title="Efik language">Efik language</a> for the 1937 film <a href="/wiki/King_Solomon%27s_Mines_(1937_film)" title="King Solomon's Mines (1937 film)"><i>King Solomon's Mines</i></a>? <small>"There is, for instance, E. I. Ekpenyon, an ebony-black Efik frim Nigeria, who coaches Paul Robeson in the Efik speeches of the picture" from: 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation news cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.newspapers.com/clip/78498859/">"Negro Scholar in New British Film"</a>. <i>Star-Phoenix</i>. 7 November 1936. p.&nbsp;4<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">28 May</span> 2021</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Star-Phoenix&amp;rft.atitle=Negro+Scholar+in+New+British+Film&amp;rft.pages=4&amp;rft.date=1936-11-07&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.newspapers.com%2Fclip%2F78498859%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know" class="Z3988"></span></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Ita_Ekpenyon" title="Ita Ekpenyon">Ita Ekpenyon</a></b> is "among the most well-known of the black people who experienced <a href="/wiki/The_Blitz" title="The Blitz">the Blitz</a>"? <small>"One of a small community of only 15,000 Londoners of African origin, Ita is among the most well-known of the black people who experienced the Blitz, largely because he wrote a memoir of his service." from: 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFWorsley2021" class="citation news cs1">Worsley, Lucy (5 February 2021). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.historyextra.com/period/second-world-war/lucy-worsley-blitz-stories/">"Lucy Worsley on Blitz Spirit: the courageous stories of six Londoners"</a>. <i>HistoryExtra</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">28 May</span> 2021</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=HistoryExtra&amp;rft.atitle=Lucy+Worsley+on+Blitz+Spirit%3A+the+courageous+stories+of+six+Londoners&amp;rft.date=2021-02-05&amp;rft.aulast=Worsley&amp;rft.aufirst=Lucy&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.historyextra.com%2Fperiod%2Fsecond-world-war%2Flucy-worsley-blitz-stories%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know" class="Z3988"></span></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Buddha-like_mindset">Buddha-like mindset</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FBuddha-like_mindset&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Buddha-like_mindset&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that in China, <b><a href="/wiki/Buddha-like_mindset" title="Buddha-like mindset">Buddha-like parents</a></b>, the polar opposite of <a href="/wiki/Tiger_parenting" title="Tiger parenting">tiger parents</a>, do not envision their offspring's accomplishing much in life? 
        <div style="font-size:smaller">
         Sources: 
         <ol>
          <li>
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFLi2019" class="citation journal cs1">Li, Ping (2019). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20210601042157/https://aeescience.org/uploads/ppapers/2019093001ALAC2019/ALAC93008.pdf">"A Cognitive Interpretation of Chinese Neologism Foxi"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i>Journal of Arts &amp; Humanities Studies</i>. The Academy of Engineering and Education. <b>1</b>: 34–37. <a href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.35532%2FJAHS.V1.008">10.35532/JAHS.V1.008</a>. <a href="/wiki/ISSN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISSN (identifier)">ISSN</a>&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/issn/2664-0295">2664-0295</a>. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://aeescience.org/uploads/ppapers/2019093001ALAC2019/ALAC93008.pdf">the original</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> on 2021-06-01<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2021-06-01</span></span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal+of+Arts+%26+Humanities+Studies&amp;rft.atitle=A+Cognitive+Interpretation+of+Chinese+Neologism+Foxi&amp;rft.volume=1&amp;rft.pages=34-37&amp;rft.date=2019&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.35532%2FJAHS.V1.008&amp;rft.issn=2664-0295&amp;rft.aulast=Li&amp;rft.aufirst=Ping&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Faeescience.org%2Fuploads%2Fppapers%2F2019093001ALAC2019%2FALAC93008.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know" class="Z3988"></span><p>The article notes: "<i>foxi fumu</i> (Buddha-like parents) ... <i>Foxi fumu</i>: parents who have low expectations of their children."</p></li>
          <li>
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFYang2021" class="citation book cs1">Yang, Jie (2021). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=joYmEAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA125">"The Rise of the Therapeutic in Contemporary China"</a>. In Minas, Harry (ed.). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=joYmEAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA134"><i>Mental Health in China and the Chinese Diaspora: Historical and Cultural Perspectives</i></a>. Cham: <a href="/wiki/Springer_Nature" title="Springer Nature">Springer Nature</a>. pp.&nbsp;134–135. <a href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1007%2F978-3-030-65161-9">10.1007/978-3-030-65161-9</a>. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-3-030-65160-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-3-030-65160-2"><bdi>978-3-030-65160-2</bdi></a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2021-06-01</span></span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=The+Rise+of+the+Therapeutic+in+Contemporary+China&amp;rft.btitle=Mental+Health+in+China+and+the+Chinese+Diaspora%3A+Historical+and+Cultural+Perspectives&amp;rft.place=Cham&amp;rft.pages=134-135&amp;rft.pub=Springer+Nature&amp;rft.date=2021&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1007%2F978-3-030-65161-9&amp;rft.isbn=978-3-030-65160-2&amp;rft.aulast=Yang&amp;rft.aufirst=Jie&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DjoYmEAAAQBAJ%26pg%3DPA125&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know" class="Z3988"></span><p>The book notes: "For example, "Buddha-like childrearing" proposes a laidback approach to parenthood, in stark contrast to the intense tiger-mom parenting that is currently popular in China."</p></li>

      <h4><span id="Fran.C3.A7oise_Hardy"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Françoise_Hardy">Françoise Hardy</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FFran%C3%A7oise_Hardy&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Fran%C3%A7oise_Hardy&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 121px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Francoise_Hardy_(1969).jpg" class="image" title="Françoise Hardy in 1969"><img alt="Françoise Hardy in 1969" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Francoise_Hardy_%281969%29.jpg/121px-Francoise_Hardy_%281969%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="121" height="161" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Francoise_Hardy_%281969%29.jpg/182px-Francoise_Hardy_%281969%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Francoise_Hardy_%281969%29.jpg/242px-Francoise_Hardy_%281969%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="600"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Françoise Hardy in 1969
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that during the 1960s, <b><a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7oise_Hardy" title="Françoise Hardy">Françoise Hardy</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> was France's most exportable female singer? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20180430034019/http://www.rfimusic.com/artist/chanson/francoise-hardy/biography.html">Radio France Internationale</a>. Quote: "Françoise soon became France’s most "exportable" female singing star."</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that during the 1960s, French singer-songwriter <b><a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7oise_Hardy" title="Françoise Hardy">Françoise Hardy</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> was wooed by musicians such as <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">the Rolling Stones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a>?</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li><small> Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://elpais.com/elpais/2015/05/01/estilo/1430482810_285095.html">El País</a>. Quote: "<i>Encandiló a Mick Jagger, Bob Dylan o Eric Clapton</i>." (in English: "She dazzled Mick Jagger, Bob Dylan or Eric Clapton")</small></li> 
       <li><small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=TWwKAQAAQBAJ">Deluxe, <i>Yé-Yé Girls of '60s French Pop</i>, 2015</a> p. 60. Quote: "Even Malcolm McLaren, the controversial Sex Pistols manager, would add to it, asserting that she represented the 'utmost of the pinup girl, pinned to the walls of every trendy pop apprentice's bedroom down in Chelsea. Many bands in their prime, like the Beatles or the Stones, dreamt of dating her."</small></li> 
       <li><small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.vogue.fr/fashion-culture/fashion-exhibitions/articles/bob-dylan-wrote-love-letters-to-francoise-hardy/62683"><i>Vogue Paris</i></a>. Quote: "Bob Dylan wrote love letters to Françoise Hardy".</small></li>
      </ul>

      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>

      <h4><span id="Ronald_Barnes_.28carillonist.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Ronald_Barnes_(carillonist)">Ronald Barnes (carillonist)</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FRonald_Barnes_%28carillonist%29&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ronald_Barnes_%28carillonist%29&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that American <a href="/wiki/Carillon" title="Carillon">carillon</a> composer <b><a href="/wiki/Ronald_Barnes_(carillonist)" title="Ronald Barnes (carillonist)">Ronald Barnes</a></b> first encountered a carillon at around the age of four? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.thediapason.com/carillon-news-50">Biography in The Diapason</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Ronald_Barnes_(carillonist)" title="Ronald Barnes (carillonist)">Ronald Barnes</a></b> was a major force in establishing an American approach to writing music for the <a href="/wiki/Carillon" title="Carillon">carillon</a>? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.gcna.org/barnes-grants">Short bio at his memorial grant page</a></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FPiano_Sonata_No._2_%28Shostakovich%29&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... ... that although he initially dismissed his own <b><a href="/wiki/Piano_Sonata_No._2_(Shostakovich)" title="Piano Sonata No. 2 (Shostakovich)">Piano Sonata No. 2</a></b> as a "trifle," <a href="/wiki/Dmitri_Shostakovich" title="Dmitri Shostakovich">Dmitri Shostakovich</a> would later consider it his most important piano composition? <small>(Source: "At the composer's express wish after discussing several projects Inger Wikström performs here his Sonata No. 2. This work, which he premiered on November 11, 1943[sic] while the war was still raging, he values most among his piano compositions." Liner notes for Swedish Society Discofil SCD 1031, page 3)</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that despite being considered one of the great exponents of <a href="/wiki/Dmitri_Shostakovich" title="Dmitri Shostakovich">Dmitri Shostakovich</a>'s <b><a href="/wiki/Piano_Sonata_No._2_(Shostakovich)" title="Piano Sonata No. 2 (Shostakovich)">Piano Sonata No. 2</a></b>, <a href="/wiki/Emil_Gilels" title="Emil Gilels">Emil Gilels</a> found the music unsatisfying? <small>Source: "Even Emil Gilels, who later became one of the Sonata's greatest exponents, felt at the time that it "testifie[d] more to Shostakovich's wonderful technique than to the depth of thought which was characteristic of his last symphonies." (A Shostakovich Companion, page 143)</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that <a href="/wiki/Dmitri_Shostakovich" title="Dmitri Shostakovich">Dmitri Shostakovich</a>'s <b><a href="/wiki/Piano_Sonata_No._2_(Shostakovich)" title="Piano Sonata No. 2 (Shostakovich)">Piano Sonata No. 2</a></b> was described by one commentator as being "something disquieting—something faintly obsessive"? <small>Source: "John Gruen notes that 'there is nothing forbidding in Shostakovich’s Second Sonata—nothing obscure or technically impenetrable about its design or content. And yet, something disquieting—something faintly obsessive—emerges from its deceptively simple structure.'" (Shostakovich's Music for Piano Solo: Interpretation and Performance, page 81)</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Philip_Ewell">Philip Ewell</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FPhilip_Ewell&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Philip_Ewell&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that music theorist <b><a href="/wiki/Philip_Ewell" title="Philip Ewell">Philip Ewell</a></b> received "anti-Black statements and personal ad hominem attacks" after his claim that Western music theory is shaped by a 'white racial frame'?</li>
      </ul> 
      <div style="font-size:85%;">
       Sources:

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Iskaq_Tjokrohadisurjo">Iskaq Tjokrohadisurjo</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FIskaq_Tjokrohadisurjo&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Iskaq_Tjokrohadisurjo&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Iskaq_Tjokrohadisurjo" title="Iskaq Tjokrohadisurjo">Iskaq Tjokrohadisurjo</a></b> founded the first <a href="/wiki/Native_Indonesians" title="Native Indonesians">native</a> law office in <a href="/wiki/Batavia,_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Batavia, Dutch East Indies">Batavia</a>? <small>Source: 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFLev1976" class="citation journal cs1"><a href="/wiki/Daniel_Lev" title="Daniel Lev">Lev, Daniel S.</a> (1976). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/stable/3350960">"Origins of the Indonesian Advocacy"</a>. <i>Indonesia</i> (21): 134–169.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Indonesia&amp;rft.atitle=Origins+of+the+Indonesian+Advocacy&amp;rft.issue=21&amp;rft.pages=134-169&amp;rft.date=1976&amp;rft.aulast=Lev&amp;rft.aufirst=Daniel+S.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.jstor.org%2Fstable%2F3350960&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know" class="Z3988"></span>, p154: "[...] an office opened by Iskaq Cokrohadisuryo in Batavia, the first Indonesian office in the colonial capital."</small></li>
      </ul>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="30_West_56th_Street">30 West 56th Street</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2F30_West_56th_Street&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=30_West_56th_Street&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 116px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Henry_Seligman_House_30_West_56th_Street.jpg" class="image" title="Henry Seligman's house at 30 West 56th Street"><img alt="Henry Seligman's house at 30 West 56th Street" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Henry_Seligman_House_30_West_56th_Street.jpg/116px-Henry_Seligman_House_30_West_56th_Street.jpg" decoding="async" width="116" height="169" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Henry_Seligman_House_30_West_56th_Street.jpg/174px-Henry_Seligman_House_30_West_56th_Street.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Henry_Seligman_House_30_West_56th_Street.jpg/232px-Henry_Seligman_House_30_West_56th_Street.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1582" data-file-height="2304"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Henry Seligman's house at 30 West 56th Street
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that banker Henry Seligman's house at <b><a href="/wiki/30_West_56th_Street" title="30 West 56th Street">30 West 56th Street</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> had a reception room with green marble furniture and a library with a Gothic-style wastebasket? <small>Source: "Experts Say That Fewer Private Houses Are Building on Manhattan at This Christmastide Than for Many Years Previous". New-York Tribune. December 21, 1902. p. B8.</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that the grand stairs in banker Henry Seligman's house at <b><a href="/wiki/30_West_56th_Street" title="30 West 56th Street">30 West 56th Street</a></b> were used mostly as decoration, since the house had an electric elevator? <small>Source: "Experts Say That Fewer Private Houses Are Building on Manhattan at This Christmastide Than for Many Years Previous". New-York Tribune. December 21, 1902. p. B8.</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that after the original residents of <b><a href="/wiki/30_West_56th_Street" title="30 West 56th Street">30 West 56th Street</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> died, in 1934, the house's dinner plates alone were sold for US$2,660.92? <small>Source: Birmingham, Stephen (2015) [1967]. Our Crowd. New York: Harper &amp; Row. p. 409</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Did you know nominations/">Template:Did you know nominations/_</a></li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: QPQ pending, more hooks later</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Zahia_Kaddoura">Zahia Kaddoura</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FZahia_Kaddoura&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Zahia_Kaddoura&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that Lebanese academic <b><a href="/wiki/Zahia_Kaddoura" title="Zahia Kaddoura">Zahia Kaddoura</a></b> was the first woman appointed as a dean at the <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_University" title="Lebanese University">Lebanese University</a>? <small>Source: "<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://pioneersandleaders.org/women-pioneers/dr-zahia-kaddoura">Dr. Zahia Kaddoura was the first woman to be appointed to a senior post in a Lebanese university in her capacity as Dean of Literature and Human Sciences</a>"</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Zahia_Kaddoura" title="Zahia Kaddoura">Zahia Kaddoura</a></b> was the first Lebanese woman to earn a PhD from an Egyptian university? <small>Source: "<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://pioneersandleaders.org/women-pioneers/dr-zahia-kaddoura">She was also the first Lebanese woman to earn a PhD from an Egyptian university. Kaddoura completed her PhD in Arabic and Islamic history in Cairo, returning to Beirut in 1951.</a>"</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Kevin_Kelley_(American_football)" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Kevin Kelley (American football)">Kevin Kelley (American football)</a></li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: Written by <a href="/wiki/User:Salukk" title="User:Salukk">Salukk</a> and moved by <a href="/wiki/User:QuakerSquirrel" title="User:QuakerSquirrel">QuakerSquirrel</a> into the mainspace on June 2, 2021.</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_Hibernian_Hotel">Royal Hibernian Hotel</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FRoyal_Hibernian_Hotel&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Royal_Hibernian_Hotel&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Royal_Hibernian_Hotel" title="Royal Hibernian Hotel">Royal Hibernian Hotel</a></b> is thought to be the oldest <s>known</s> hotel in Ireland? <small>Source: "The origin of the Royal Hibernian Hotel, Dawson Street, goes back to 1751, which makes it the oldest known hotel in Ireland. "</small></li>
      </ul><small></small>
      <p><small>(<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://arrow.tudublin.ie/cgi/viewcontent.cgi?article=1003&amp;context=hibhot">[45]</a>)</small> </p>

       <dd>
        <ul>

       </dd>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Yankee"><i>The Yankee</i></span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FThe_Yankee&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=%27%27The_Yankee%27%27&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <a href="/wiki/John_Neal_(writer)" title="John Neal (writer)">John Neal</a> vindicated himself with <i><b><a href="/wiki/The_Yankee" title="The Yankee">The Yankee</a></b></i>? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.google.com/books/edition/John_Neal/SJ6wAAAAIAAJ">this book</a> says on page 112 "As editor ... [Neal's] true reward was in earning back his place of acceptance in his hometown. Early issues, therefore, contain a good deal of self-vindication".</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that "the very first words of encouragement <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Allan_Poe" title="Edgar Allan Poe">[Poe]</a> ever remember[ed] to have heard" were in <i><b><a href="/wiki/The_Yankee" title="The Yankee">The Yankee</a></b></i>? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.google.com/books/edition/John_Neal/SJ6wAAAAIAAJ">this book</a> says on page 114 "[Edgar Allan Poe] seized on Neal's words regarding the possibilities of his writing a beautiful and perhaps magnificent poem, calling them 'the very first words of encouragement I ever remember to have heard<span style="padding-right:.15em;">'</span>".</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Portrait_of_Madame_Jacques-Louis_Leblanc" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Portrait of Madame Jacques-Louis Leblanc">Template:Did you know nominations/Portrait of Madame Jacques-Louis Leblanc</a></li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: Let me know your opinion on one hook versus the other. ALT1 seems more relevant to a wide audience given Poe's name recognition, but I like the snappy sound of the first hook. Thanks in advance for reviewing my nomination!</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Wynne_Neilly">Wynne Neilly</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FWynne_Neilly&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wynne_Neilly&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that photographing <a href="/wiki/Elliot_Page" title="Elliot Page">Elliot Page</a> for the cover of <a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)"><i>Time</i></a> "really meant the world" to Canadian photographer <b><a href="/wiki/Wynne_Neilly" title="Wynne Neilly">Wynne Neilly</a></b>? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.ryerson.ca/news-events/news/2021/04/ryerson-grad-photographs-elliot-page-in-times-first-cover-of-trans-man/">a Ryerson University interview</a>, where Neilly said that "I have so much gratitude for his choice to request me as his photographer for this historical moment. It really meant the world to me to be able to help him tell his story and that he trusted me to do it right. It felt like a lot of pressure but at the same time I knew I was the right fit and I knew I could deliver."</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that inspirations for <b><a href="/wiki/Wynne_Neilly" title="Wynne Neilly">Wynne Neilly</a></b><span class="nowrap">'s</span> photography of queer and transgender people include <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Opie" title="Catherine Opie">Catherine Opie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cassils_(artist)" title="Cassils (artist)">Cassils</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Groskopf" title="Michelle Groskopf">Michelle Groskopf</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mapplethorpe" title="Robert Mapplethorpe">Robert Mapplethorpe</a>? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.sissyscreens.com/something-to-talk-about-wynne-neilly-photography-series/">This interview</a>, where Neilly said that "Catherine Opie would be my number one photographic inspiration. I am really inspired by artists working closely with their communities and who use their body to tell a story. Some other inspirations of mine right now include: Cassils, Robert Coombs, Michelle Groskopf, Brene Brown, Robert Mapplethrope, Landon Speers, @shooglet, my community and dadaism. I’m also very into architecture right now, especially brutalist style architecture."</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Obed_Dickinson" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Obed Dickinson">Obed Dickinson</a></li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: It'd be lovely if this could run in June for pride month.</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="William_E._Woods">William E. Woods</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FWilliam_E._Woods&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=William_E._Woods&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the only two names mentioned in conservative activist <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Falwell_Sr." title="Jerry Falwell Sr.">Jerry Falwell</a><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> farewell speech after his truncated 1981 trip to Hawaii were <a href="/wiki/William_E._Woods" title="William E. Woods"><b>Bill Woods</b></a> and Jesus Christ? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.politico.com/news/magazine/2021/05/31/issenberg-book-excerpt-bill-woods-honolulu-doma-491401">Politico</a>, "When conservative televangelist Jerry Falwell traveled to Hawaii in May 1981 [...] Woods led a group that beat him to register the name with state authorities [...] When he held a rally outside the state capitol in Honolulu, Falwell was confronted by a sheriff presenting him with a summons: the Moral Majority of Hawaii was suing his Moral Majority, Inc. for using its name. Concerned they could get ensnared in the litigation, other venues which had agreed to host stops on Falwell’s Hawaii tour cancelled. Before retreating back to Virginia, a disconsolate Falwell gave a farewell speech that mentioned only two names: Jesus Christ and Bill Woods."</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that after <b><a href="/wiki/William_E._Woods" title="William E. Woods">William E. Woods</a></b> cut short a 1981 trip to Hawaii by <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Falwell_Sr." title="Jerry Falwell Sr.">Jerry Falwell Sr.</a>, the only two people mentioned in Falwell's farewell speech were Woods and Jesus Christ? <small>Source: See ALT0</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/William_E._Woods" title="William E. Woods">William E. Woods</a></b> took three <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_couples" class="mw-redirect" title="Same-sex couples">same-sex couples</a> to fill out <a href="/wiki/Marriage_license" title="Marriage license">marriage licenses</a> in 1990, beginning a series of events that would lead to the legalization of <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_United_States" title="Same-sex marriage in the United States">same-sex marriage in the United States</a>? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.politico.com/news/magazine/2021/05/31/issenberg-book-excerpt-bill-woods-honolulu-doma-491401">Politico</a>, "Bill Woods had plans to make news, not history. He would bring three same-sex couples, two female and one male, to the main office of the Hawaii Department of Public Health in downtown Honolulu, where they would complete applications for marriage licenses. [...] What they had done was set in motion a chain of events that would send a novel legal question from the outskirts of the American imagination to the floor of Congress and the Oval Office in a little more than five years. Within a quarter-century, the U.S. Supreme Court would end the debate for good."</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Whistle_Belly_Vengeance">Whistle Belly Vengeance</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FWhistle_Belly_Vengeance&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Whistle_Belly_Vengeance&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that late arrivals to <a href="/wiki/Colonial_history_of_the_United_States" title="Colonial history of the United States">American colonial era</a> inns might find the only drink on offer was <b><a href="/wiki/Whistle_Belly_Vengeance" title="Whistle Belly Vengeance">Whistle Belly Vengeance</a></b>; a mixture of sour beer, molasses and bread crusts? <small>"Hungry guests , arriving late at night at a wayside inn , might have to make do with a formidable concoction known as “ whistle - belly - vengeance , ” consisting of household beer , with crusts of brown bread - rye - and - Injun - crumbled in and the whole sweetened with molasses" from: 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation book cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.google.co.uk/books/edition/Taverns_of_Yesteryear/IHFNAQAAMAAJ"><i>Taverns of Yesteryear</i></a>. C. Schmidt &amp; Sons. 1960. p.&nbsp;19.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Taverns+of+Yesteryear&amp;rft.pages=19&amp;rft.pub=C.+Schmidt+%26+Sons&amp;rft.date=1960&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.google.co.uk%2Fbooks%2Fedition%2FTaverns_of_Yesteryear%2FIHFNAQAAMAAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know" class="Z3988"></span></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that American patriot <a href="/wiki/James_Otis_Jr." title="James Otis Jr.">James Otis Jr.</a> was so fond of one Boston coffee house's <b><a href="/wiki/Whistle_Belly_Vengeance" title="Whistle Belly Vengeance">Whistle Belly Vengeance</a></b> that he continued to drink there after it had ben taken over by British soldiers? <small>"The ever changeable , moody and nervous Jimmy Otis enjoyed eating and drinking everywhere. Even though the British had taken over the Royal Coffee House , he still enjoyed their special sour - beer and rum drink mix called a " Whistle Belly Vengeance , ” so he continued to frequent the place" from: 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFCahill1987" class="citation book cs1">Cahill, Robert (1987). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.google.co.uk/books/edition/New_England_s_Riotous_Revolution/qIZ4AAAAMAAJ"><i>New England's Riotous Revolution</i></a>. Chandler-Smith. p.&nbsp;25. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-916787-12-7" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-916787-12-7"><bdi>978-0-916787-12-7</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=New+England%27s+Riotous+Revolution&amp;rft.pages=25&amp;rft.pub=Chandler-Smith&amp;rft.date=1987&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-916787-12-7&amp;rft.aulast=Cahill&amp;rft.aufirst=Robert&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.google.co.uk%2Fbooks%2Fedition%2FNew_England_s_Riotous_Revolution%2FqIZ4AAAAMAAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know" class="Z3988"></span></small></li>

      <h4><span id="Hierocracy_.28medieval.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Hierocracy_(medieval)">Hierocracy (medieval)</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FHierocracy_%28medieval%29&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hierocracy_%28medieval%29&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the 14th-century <b><a href="/wiki/Hierocracy_(medieval)" title="Hierocracy (medieval)">hierocrats</a></b> thought the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">pope</a> was the rightful <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereign</a> of the entire world? <small>Source: "By the beginning of the 14th century&nbsp;... Giles, James, and Henry produced the ultimate and unambiguous hierocratic claim of universal papal monarchy with the pope as the <i>de iure</i> ruler of the entire world." (<i>A Companion to the Medieval Papacy</i>, p. 131: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.google.co.uk/books/edition/A_Companion_to_the_Medieval_Papacy/2n8JDAAAQBAJ?hl=en&amp;gbpv=1&amp;pg=PA131&amp;printsec=frontcover">Google Books</a>, bottom paragraph)</small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Pre-Socratic_philosophy" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Pre-Socratic philosophy">Pre-Socratic philosophy</a></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FWBPX-TV&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

      </dl> 
      <h4><span id="Steve_Bennett_.28California_politician.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Steve_Bennett_(California_politician)">Steve Bennett (California politician)</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FSteve_Bennett_%28California_politician%29&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Steve_Bennett_%28California_politician%29&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Steve_Bennett_(California_politician)" title="Steve Bennett (California politician)">Steve Bennett</a></b><span class="nowrap">'s</span> write-in candidacy for city council was endorsed by <a href="/wiki/Patagonia,_Inc." title="Patagonia, Inc.">Patagonia, Inc.</a>? <small>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation news cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.newspapers.com/clip/78947076/the-los-angeles-times/">"Patagonia Endorses Villeneuve, Bennett"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i>. October 11, 1991. p.&nbsp;464. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.ph/xxBNH">Archived</a> from the original on June 4, 2021 – via <a href="/wiki/Newspapers.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Newspapers.com">Newspapers.com</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Los+Angeles+Times&amp;rft.atitle=Patagonia+Endorses+Villeneuve%2C+Bennett&amp;rft.pages=464&amp;rft.date=1991-10-11&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.newspapers.com%2Fclip%2F78947076%2Fthe-los-angeles-times%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know" class="Z3988"></span></small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: TBA</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p><small>5x expanded by <a href="/wiki/User:Jon698" title="User:Jon698">Jon698</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Jon698" title="User talk:Jon698">talk</a>). Self-nominated at 16:09, 5 June 2021 (UTC).</small> </p>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cal_Anderson">Cal Anderson</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FCal_Anderson&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cal_Anderson&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Cal_Anderson" title="Cal Anderson">Cal Anderson</a></b> was the first openly gay member of the <a href="/wiki/Washington_State_Legislature" title="Washington State Legislature">Washington State Legislature</a>? <small>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation news cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.historylink.org/File/10265">"Anderson, Cal (1948-1995)"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/HistoryLink" title="HistoryLink">HistoryLink</a></i>. December 26, 2012. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.ph/iWZV2">Archived</a> from the original on June 2, 2021.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=HistoryLink&amp;rft.atitle=Anderson%2C+Cal+%281948-1995%29&amp;rft.date=2012-12-26&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.historylink.org%2FFile%2F10265&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know" class="Z3988"></span></small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: TBA</li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: Can this be put on the main page before June ends since it is Pride month?</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p><small>5x expanded by <a href="/wiki/User:Jon698" title="User:Jon698">Jon698</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Jon698" title="User talk:Jon698">talk</a>). Self-nominated at 16:07, 5 June 2021 (UTC).</small> </p>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Raychell">Raychell</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FRaychell&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Raychell&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Raychell" title="Raychell">Raychell</a></b><span class="nowrap">'s</span> previous stage name Lay was meant to represent her belief that singing while lying down would heal listeners? <small>Source: ROCK AND READ girls (in Japanese). Shinko Music Entertainment. May 25, 2019. p. 104.</small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Embassy_of_the_Philippines,_The_Hague" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Embassy of the Philippines, The Hague">Template:Did you know nominations/Embassy of the Philippines, The Hague ?</a></li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: Unfortunately I have no access to the source used in the article as the relevant passage was translated from the Japanese article, but the reference is there too and I am assuming good faith on its veracity. Inviting <a href="/wiki/User:ZappaOMatic" title="User:ZappaOMatic">ZappaOMatic</a> to expand the article and potentially suggest additional hooks as well.</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p><small>Created by <a href="/wiki/User:Narutolovehinata5" title="User:Narutolovehinata5">Narutolovehinata5</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Narutolovehinata5" title="User talk:Narutolovehinata5">talk</a>). Self-nominated at 04:03, 5 June 2021 (UTC).</small> </p>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Indrani">Indrani</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FIndrani&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Indrani&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Indrani" title="Indrani">Indrani</a></b>, the queen of Hindu <a href="/wiki/Deva_(Hinduism)" title="Deva (Hinduism)">devas</a> (gods), is a daughter of a <a href="/wiki/Asura" title="Asura">demonic figure</a>? Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://books.google.co.in/books?id=1HMXN9h6WX0C&amp;q=Indra+wife&amp;pg=RA1-PA260&amp;redir_esc=y#v=snippet&amp;q=Indr%C4%81%E1%B9%87%C4%AB%20demon&amp;f=false">[53]</a> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... In Hindu mythology, a king named <a href="/wiki/Nahusha" title="Nahusha">Nahusha</a> was turned into a snake after he desired for <b><a href="/wiki/Indrani" title="Indrani">Indrani</a></b>, the wife of the god <a href="/wiki/Indra" title="Indra">Indra</a>&nbsp;? Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://books.google.co.in/books?id=5kl0DYIjUPgC&amp;q=indrani+indrajita&amp;pg=PA297&amp;redir_esc=y#v=snippet&amp;q=indrani%20indrajita&amp;f=false">[54]</a></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p><small>Improved to Good Article status by <a href="/wiki/User:245CMR" title="User:245CMR">245CMR</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:245CMR" title="User talk:245CMR">talk</a>). Self-nominated at 12:43, 5 June 2021 (UTC).</small> </p>

       <dd>

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_June_6"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_June_6">Articles created/expanded on June 6</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on June 6">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_occasion_holding_area">Special occasion holding area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Special occasion holding area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p><b>The holding area has moved</b> to its new location at the bottom of the <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved#Special_occasion_holding_area" title="Template talk:Did you know/Approved">Approved page</a>. Please only place approved templates there; do not place them below. </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>Do <b>not</b> nominate articles in this section—nominate all articles in the <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Did_you_know#Nominations" title="Template talk:Did you know">nominations</a> section above, under the date on which the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:DYKTN#article" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:DYKTN">article</a> was created or moved to mainspace, or the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:DYKTN#expansion" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:DYKTN">expansion</a> began; indicate in the nomination any request for a specially timed appearance on the main page.</i>
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        <i>Note: Articles intended to be held for special occasion dates should be nominated within seven days of creation, start of expansion, or promotion to Good Article status. The nomination should be made at least one week prior to the occasion date, to allow time for reviews and promotions through the prep and queue sets, but not more than six weeks in advance. The proposed occasion must be deemed sufficiently special by reviewers. The timeline limitations, including the six week maximum, may be waived by consensus, if a request is made at <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia_talk:DYK" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia talk:DYK">WT:DYK</a>, but requests are not always successful. Discussion clarifying the hold criteria can be found here: <a class="external autonumber" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia_talk:Did_you_know#Revision_3">[55]</a>; discussion setting the six week limit can be found here: <a class="external autonumber" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia_talk:Did_you_know/Archive_65#Rhacophorus_vampyrus">[56]</a>.</i>
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        <i>April Fools' Day hooks are exempted from the timeline limit; see <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:April_Fool%27s_Main_Page/Did_You_Know" title="Wikipedia:April Fool's Main Page/Did You Know">Wikipedia:April Fool's Main Page/Did You Know</a></b>.</i>
       </dd>
      </dl> <!--
